Buyu — Sales and Trade

12 min
Khiyar al-Shart: Definition, Proof, and Usul Analysis
Explains definition, proof, legal theory of khiyar al-shart as man'i, and lists eight types of khiyar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and proof of khiyar al-shart, explain the Hanafi usul position on man'i, and list the eight types of khiyar in sale.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is valid by text, delaying ownership; it is not a preventer but an incomplete cause.

This lesson opens the chapter on khiyar al-shart from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author first defines the term and establishes its textual basis, then engages in a nuanced usul discussion about how the option affects the contract's legal cause ('illah). He rejects the common classification of khiyar as a 'preventer' (mani') and instead argues that the option renders the cause incomplete. Finally, he lists eight types of khiyar, showing the breadth of the school's treatment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that khiyar al-shart is a stipulated option allowing cancellation or confirmation, and that it delays ownership transfer.
2
Locate the dalil
Note that the option is established by a textual proof (النص) despite being contrary to analogy (على غير القياس).
The specific text is not quoted here; the author assumes familiarity.
3
Understand the usul theory
The option enters upon the hukm (ruling), not the contract itself, thus delaying the effect of the sale.
The author contrasts this with a prohibition of 'sale with a condition' in a certain sense.
4
Analyze the dispute on man'i
Some usuliyyun classify preventers into five types and place khiyar al-shart as man'i ibtida' al-hukm. The author refutes this based on the principle that 'illah cannot be specified.
On the correct view, the absence of hukm is due to incomplete 'illah, not a preventer.
5
Know the eight types
The author lists eight types of khiyar, beyond the commonly known three (khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-'ayb).
These include khiyar al-ghabn, khiyar al-kammiyyah, khiyar al-istihqaq, khiyar kashf al-hal, and khiyar tafarrq al-safqah.

It is from adding the thing to its cause because the condition is a cause for the option. And in al-Misbah: al-khiyar and al-ikhtiyar. And he explained it in Fath al-Bari as choosing between execution and cancellation, and it is established by text contrary to analogy. When the text came with it, we made it enter upon the ruling as a preventer for it, reducing its operation as much as possible, and we did not make it enter upon the original sale due to the prohibition of a sale with a condition. And the sale in which the option is stipulated is said to have a cause in name not in effect, and the one free from it has a cause in name and effect. The scholars of usul said: Preventers. The meaning of preventer of the conclusion of the cause is the freedom of the sold item, so it is not concluded in a free person due to lack of subject. And a preventer that prevents its completion like the sale of another's property. And a preventer that prevents the inception of the ruling and it is the option of stipulation. And a preventer that prevents its completion like the option of sight for the buyer. And a preventer that prevents its bindingness like the option of defect. And we have verified in our commentary on al-Manar that their division of preventers is based on a weak view of the usuliyyun, which is the permissibility of specifying causes. As for the correct view that it is not permissible to specify them, there is no preventer for them at all. So in every place where the ruling is absent, it is due to the absence of the cause. Thus, the delay of ownership with the option of stipulation is only due to the absence of the cause because it is the sale without an option. And their statement that in what has an option, cause in name and meaning not in effect is metaphorical according to the correct view because what exists is a part of the cause, not all of it, because it is not complete except with three attributes: that it be established, that it be effective, and that the ruling follows it without delay. As long as the option remains, the cause is not complete; when it drops, it is complete. And its completion is in the exposition of al-Akmal in the discussion of dividing causes into seven. And the options in sale are not limited to three as we have mentioned, but rather they are options. The fourth is the option of fraud and we will discuss it in the chapter of murabahah where they mentioned it. The fifth is the option of quantity and we mentioned it at the beginning of sales. The sixth is the option of eviction and it will come in the chapter of option of defect. The seventh is the option of investigation of the situation as we have mentioned. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation). The author first defines the term: it is an option that arises from a condition stipulated by one of the parties, literally meaning 'choice.' It is established by a textual proof (النص) despite being contrary to analogy (على غير القياس), meaning that normally a sale would be immediately binding, but the option is allowed by exception. The author explains that the option enters upon the ruling (حكم) of the contract, preventing its effect, not upon the contract itself, because of the prohibition of 'a sale with a condition' in a certain sense. He then delves into the usul theory of man'i (preventers). According to some usuliyyun, there are five types of man'i: man'i al-in'iqaad (preventing the conclusion), man'i al-tamām (preventing completion), man'i ibtida' al-hukm (preventing the inception of the ruling), man'i tamām al-hukm (preventing the completion of the ruling), and man'i luzūm (preventing bindingness). They place khiyar al-shart as the third type, preventing the inception of the ruling. However, the author refutes this, stating that this classification is based on a weak usuli view that allows takhsis al-'ilal (specification of causes). On the correct view, there is no man'i at all; rather, the ruling is absent due to the incompleteness of the 'illah. The 'illah for ownership is a sale without an option. When an option is present, the 'illah is not fully realized because it requires three attributes: being established (موضوعة), being effective (مؤثرة), and that the hukm follows without delay. While the option exists, the 'illah is incomplete; when the option expires, the 'illah is complete and ownership follows. The author then lists eight types of khiyar in sales: 1) khiyar al-shart, 2) khiyar al-ghabn (fraud), 3) khiyar al-kammiyyah (quantity), 4) khiyar al-istihqaq (eviction), 5) khiyar kashf al-hal (investigation), 6) khiyar tafarrq al-safqah (separation of transaction due to destruction of part before possession), and others. He notes that the commonly known three (khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-'ayb) are not exhaustive. This passage is a blend of fiqh and usul al-fiqh, demonstrating the rigour of Hanafi legal theory.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by the parties to a sale contract allowing either to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period.
مانع (mani'): In usul al-fiqh, a preventer that either prevents the 'illah from producing its hukm or prevents the hukm itself from taking effect.
علة (‘illah): The effective cause that necessitates the hukm; in this context, the sale contract is the 'illah for ownership.
تخصيص العلل (takhsis al-'ilal): The concept that the 'illah can be specified or excluded in certain cases, allowing the hukm not to apply despite the presence of the 'illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many types of khiyar (options) are mentioned in sale beyond the initial three?
A) 3
B) 5
C) 8
D) 7

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is a valid option established by text, and its effect is to delay the completion of the legal cause of ownership, not to act as a preventer.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Ruling and Proof of Khiyar al-Shart
Ruling with proof, usul analysis on preventers, and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al‑shart, identify its proof from the hadith of Habban ibn Munqidh, and explain how it functions as a preventer (mani‛) that delays the completion of the cause of ownership.

Core Idea
A sale with a stipulated option for up to three days is valid, but ownership does not transfer until the option period ends.

This passage from al‑Bahr al‑Ra’iq opens the chapter on khiyar al‑shart—the option that arises from a stipulation in the contract. The commentator first clarifies the nature of khiyar as a preventer (mani‛) that delays the ruling, then presents the hadith proof, and finally discusses the maximum period and who may stipulate it. Understanding this foundation is essential because it shapes how the Hanafi school treats conditional sales.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the ruling and its grammatical nuance
The text says 'صح للمتبايعين أو لأحدهما ثلاثة أيام'. Identify what 'sahha' refers to: the option (khiyar) or the stipulation (shart)? Note the preferred view in al‑Islah that it is the stipulation that is valid.
This nuance affects how we analyze the cause (illah) and the preventer.
2
2. Understand the preventer (mani‛) framework
The commentator explains that khiyar is a mani‛ that prevents the completion of the illah (cause) of ownership. Review the five types of preventers and note that khiyar al‑shart prevents the initiation of the ruling (ownership).
The correct view is that the illah is incomplete as long as the option remains.
3
3. Locate and analyse the proof (dalil naqli)
The hadith of Habban ibn Munqidh from Sunan Ibn Majah. Extract the key phrase: 'then you have in every commodity you purchase the option for three nights'. Note that the option is mentioned for the buyer, but the Hanafis extend it to the seller based on the general instruction 'when you sell'.
The hadith also contains the recommended phrase 'la khilabah'.
4
4. Apply the conditions
The option period is a maximum of three days; if stipulated for longer, the condition is invalid. The option can be for both parties or one. Dropping parts of the period has specific rules (e.g., dropping the first day voids all).
The default is that the contract is binding; options are exceptions.

باب خيار الشرط
من إضافة الشيء إلى سببه لأن الشرط سبب للخيار. وفي المصباح: الخيار والاختيار. وفسره في فتح الباري بالتخيير بين الإمضاء والفسخ وهو ثابت بالنص على غير القياس وحين ورد النص به جعلناه داخلاً على الحكم مانعاً له تقليلاً لعمله بقدر الإمكان، ولم نجعله داخلاً على أصل البيع للنهي عن بيع بشرط والبيع الذي شرط فيه الخيار يقال فيه علة اسماً لا حكماً، وللخالي عنه علة اسماً خمسة : وحكماً. قال أهل الأصول: الموانع ومعنى مانع انعقاد العلة وهو حرية المبيع فلم ينعقد في الحر لعدم المحل ومانع يمنع تمامها كبيع مال الغير، ومانع يمنع ابتداء الحكم وهو خيار الشرط، ومانع يمنع تمامه كخيار الرؤية للمشتري، ومانع يمنع لزومه كخيار العيب. وقد حققنا في شرحنا على المنار أن تقسيمهم الموانع مبني على قول ضعيف للأصوليين وهو جواز تخصيص العلل، وأما على الصحيح من أنه لا يجوز تخصيصها فلا مانع لها أصلاً ففي كل موضع عدم الحكم فإنما هو لعدم العلة فتخلف الملك مع شرط الخيار إنما هو لعدم العلة لأنها البيع بلا خيار، وقولهم فيما فيه خيار علة اسماً ومعنى لا حكماً مجاز على الصحيح لأن الموجود فيه شرط العلة لا كلها لأنها لا تتم إلا بأوصاف ثلاثة أن تكون موضوعة، وأن تكون مؤثرة، وأن يوجد الحكم عقبها بلا تراخ. فما دام الخيار باقياً لم تتم العلة فإذا سقط تمت وتمامه في تقرير الأكمل في بحث تقسيم العلل إلى سبعة. والخيارات في البيع لا تنحصر في الثلاثة كما قدمناه بل هي خياراً. والرابع خيار الغبن وسنتكلم عليه في المرابحة حيث ذكروه هناك. والخامس خيار الكمية وقدمناه أول البيوع والسادس خيار الاستحقاق وسيأتي في باب خيار العيب. والسابع خيار كشف الحال كما قدمناه والثامن خيار تفرق الصفقة بهلاك البعض قبل القبض

أي العاقد ـ لا خلابة بكسر الخاء • عبارة في الشرع عن اشتراط خيار الثلاث ومعناها لا غبن ولا خديعة فإن أطلقاها عالمين لا جاهلين ولا جاهل أحدهما معناها صح أي ثبت الخيار وإن أسقط من شرط له الخيار ثلاثة أيام خيار اليوم الأول بطل الكل. قال في المجموع : وإن أسقط خيار الثالث لم يسقط ما قبله أو خيار الثاني بشرط أن يبقى خيار الثالث سقط خيار اليومين جميعاً لأنه كما لا يجوز أن يشرط خياراً متراخياً عن يجوز أن يستبقي خياراً متراخياً. وإنما أسقطنا اليومين تغليباً للإسقاط لأن الأصل لزوم العقد، وإنما العقد لا
Chapter on the Option of Stipulation. It is of the addition of a thing to its cause because the stipulation is the cause of the option. In al-Misbah: al-khiyar and al-ikhtiyar. And it was explained in Fath al-Bari as the choice between ratification and rescission. It is established by text (nass) against analogy. When the text came with it, we made it enter upon the ruling (hukm) as a preventer (mani') of it, minimizing its operation as much as possible, and we did not make it enter upon the origin of the sale due to the prohibition of selling with a condition. The sale in which the option is stipulated is said to have a cause ('illa) in name, not in ruling. And that which is free of it has a cause in name and ruling. The scholars of usul said: the preventers (mawani') meaning a preventer of the conclusion of the cause is the freedom of the sold item, so it does not conclude in a free person due to lack of locus. And a preventer prevents its completion like selling the property of another. And a preventer prevents the initiation of the ruling, which is the option of stipulation. And a preventer prevents its completion like the option of sight for the buyer. And a preventer prevents its bindingness like the option of defect. We have verified in our commentary on al-Manar that their division of preventers is based on a weak opinion of the usuliyyun, which is the permissibility of specifying ('illa) causes. As for the correct view that it is not permissible to specify them, then there is no preventer for them at all. So in every place where the ruling is absent, it is due to the absence of the cause. Thus the withholding of ownership with the stipulation of an option is only due to the absence of the cause, because it is a sale without an option. And their statement that in what has an option there is a cause in name and meaning but not in ruling is a metaphor according to the correct view, because what exists in it is a condition of the cause, not all of it, because it is not completed except with three attributes: that it is established, that it is effective, and that the ruling occurs immediately after it without delay. So as long as the option remains, the cause is not completed; when it falls, it is completed. Its completion is in the discourse of al-Akmal in the section on division of causes into seven. And the options in sale are not limited to three as we have mentioned, rather they are... The fourth is the option of deception (khiyar al-ghabn) and we will discuss it in Murabaha where they mentioned it. The fifth is the option of quantity, and we mentioned it at the beginning of sales. The sixth is the option of eviction (khiyar al-istihqaq) and it will come in the chapter on the option of defect. The seventh is the option of disclosure of the condition (khiyar kashf al-hal) as we mentioned. The eighth is the option of separation of the contract due to the destruction of part before possession. Chapter on the Option of Stipulation — thirteen types. Stone. His saying: (And the seventh is the option of disclosure of the condition as we mentioned). Al-Ramli said: He presented it in the explanation of his saying 'or it is not known its value' with his saying after he said 'if he buys with the weight of this stone gold then informs him of it, it is permissible and he has the option' — and this... Book of Sales — Chapter on the Option of Stipulation. It is valid for both sellers and buyers or for one of them for three days; if more, not. So if he ratifies within the three, it is valid even if he sold. And it will come also. The ninth is the option of ratification of the contract of the intermediary (al-fuduli). The tenth is the option of the loss of the stipulated description that is due by contract, like stipulating that he is literate. The eleventh is the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin). The twelfth in Murabaha is the option of betrayal (khiyar al-khiyanah). The thirteenth of the options is the option of payment of the price and its non-payment as will come in this chapter. His saying: (It is valid for both sellers and buyers or for one of them for three days) meaning it is permissible for the seller and buyer together or for one of them in the mentioned period. And the apparent is that the pronoun refers to the option. In al-Wiqayah and al-Nifayah: 'The option of stipulation is valid' so he brought it out. And the better is what is in al-Islah: 'The stipulation of the option is valid' because the one described with validity is the stipulation of the option, not the option itself. And the basis for its establishment is what Ibn Majah narrated in his Sunan: that Habban ibn Munqidh was a man whose head was struck with a wound (ummah) that broke his teeth, and he did not cease trading despite that. He was always being cheated. So he came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and mentioned that to him. He (peace be upon him) said: 'When you sell, say: no deception (la khilabah). Then you have in every commodity you purchase the option for three nights. If you are pleased, keep it; if you are displeased, return it to its owner.' Habban is with a fatha on the ha and a shadda on the ba. Al-khilabah is deception. The benefit of his saying 'la khilabah' is: no deception in the religion because the religion is sincerity, and to inform that he is not among those who have insight into goods, so it is obligatory to advise him; do not deceive him with something relying on his knowledge, rather advise him because he is not knowledgeable of it. Thus in Fath al-Bari. Al-ummah is a wound that strikes the mother of the head. Habban had a lisp with the letter lam, so he used to say 'la khadhabah'. His saying 'when you sell' includes the seller and the buyer, and with it the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri is repelled, that only the option of disclosure of the condition is permissible, as we presented in the issue of the ditch and the buried treasure. His saying: (And the apparent is that the pronoun...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: the pronoun in 'sahha' refers to the mudaf ilayh by the context of 'sahha'. Indeed the author clarified it in Khul' where he said: 'And the stipulation of the option for her in khul' is valid, not for him.' And whoever is heedless of this says what he said. End quote. In Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud from al-Hamawi: the first is to make the pronoun refer to the option considering it as described by being stipulated before the idafah, for the idafah of option to stipulation is of the described to the attribute, not of the attribute. It does not contradict their saying that it is addition of the ruling to its cause, and the origin is the chapter on the stipulated option, with the masdar in the sense of the passive participle. That indicates that what is described with validity is not the option only as implied by the speech of Sadr al-Shari'ah, nor the stipulation only as implied by the speech of the author of al-Islah. His saying: (And al-khilabah...) Al-Ramli said: Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyya mentioned in Sharh al-Rawd here branches that our principles do not reject. He said: Branch: His saying — i.e., the contracting party — 'la khilabah' with a kasra on the kha is a phrase in the Shari'ah for stipulating the option of three, and its meaning is no defraud and no deception. If they utter it while knowing, not ignorant, nor one of them ignorant, its meaning is established (sahha) i.e., the option is proven. And if one who has the option for three days drops the option of the first day, all is void. He said in al-Majmu': If he drops the option of the third, what preceded it does not drop; or the option of the second, on condition that the option of the third remains, the option of both days drops, because just as it is not permissible to stipulate a delayed option, so it is not permissible to retain a delayed option. We dropped the two days to give weight to the dropping because the origin is the binding nature of the contract, and the contract does not...
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is from 'Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' commentary on 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq' discussing the chapter on the Option of Stipulation (khiyar al-shart). The commentator begins by explaining the term: 'khiyar' means choice, and it is defined in Fath al-Bari as the option between ratification (imda') and rescission (faskh). He notes that khiyar is established by textual evidence (nass) and is contrary to the principle of qiyas (analogy), but once the text came, it was made to enter upon the ruling as a 'mani'' (preventer) to limit its operation. The commentator then discusses the classification of mawani' (preventers) from usul al-fiqh, stating that the division into five types is based on a weak opinion allowing specification of 'illa (cause). According to the correct view (that 'illa cannot be specified), whenever the ruling (like transfer of ownership) does not occur, it is because the complete 'illa is not present. The 'illa for ownership is a sale without an option; if an option is stipulated, the 'illa is incomplete. He then lists thirteen types of options in sale, beyond the commonly known three. The key ruling is: 'It is valid for both sellers and buyers or for one of them for three days; if more, not.' The commentator clarifies that the pronoun in 'sahha' (it is valid) has been debated: does it refer to the option (khiyar) or the stipulation (shart)? He argues that the stipulation is what is described as valid. The basis for the three-day option is the hadith of Habban ibn Munqidh, who was frequently cheated in trade due to a head injury. The Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed him to say 'la khilabah' (no deception) and granted him the option for three nights. The phrase 'la khilabah' serves as a declaration that the seller should not be deceived; it also implies that the option is stipulated. The passage concludes with a discussion on dropping parts of the three-day option: if one drops the option of the first day, the entire option becomes void (since the option is continuous); dropping the third day leaves the prior options; dropping the second while keeping the third voids the second but not the third? Actually it says dropping the second on condition that the third remains drops both days? The text from al-Majmu' states: if he drops the option of the third, what preceded it does not drop; if he drops the option of the second with the condition that the third remains, both days drop. This is because it is not permissible to retain a delayed option (khiyar mutarakhi). The dropping of the two days is a 'taghlib' (giving weight) to the cancellation, as the default is that the contract is binding. The Hanafi position is that the option is valid for up to three days, for both parties or one, and it is a preventer of the binding effect of the sale. The relied-upon view is that the stipulation itself is what is valid, and the option is established by it. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as the hadith is sound and the ruling is established from the primary sources.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option that arises from a stipulation in the contract, allowing one or both parties to annul the sale within a specified period (max 3 days).
الخيار (al-khiyar): The right to choose between ratifying or rescinding a contract.
لا خلابة (la khilabah): An expression meaning 'no deception' used by the person with the option to indicate that they are not being cheated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum duration for khiyar al‑shart in the Hanafi school?
A) One day
B) Three days
C) Seven days
D) No limit

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al‑shart is valid for three days, established by the hadith of Habban ibn Munqidh, and functions as a preventer that delays ownership transfer until the option ends.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
The Validity of Khiyar al-Shart: Ruling and Proof
Commentary on the matn ruling of khiyar al-shart with proof from hadith and grammatical analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that khiyar al-shart is valid for up to three days and explain its proof from the hadith of Hibban ibn Munqidh.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is valid for three days, based on the Prophet's instruction to the cheated buyer.

In the Hanafi school, the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) is a well-known license that allows a buyer or seller to rescind a contract within a specified period. This lesson examines the primary ruling and its foundation in the Sunnah. The commentary by Ibn Nujaym clarifies the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and provides the hadith evidence, along with a subtle grammatical discussion about the wording of the matn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The matn states that it is valid for the two contracting parties or one of them to stipulate three days. This is the basic ruling: khiyar al-shart for up to three days is valid (sahih).
The option can be for both parties or just one.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Hibban ibn Munqidh from Sunan Ibn Majah. Read the hadith in the source and note the key phrase: 'you have the option for three nights'.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in this context.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit instruction 'then you have the option... for three nights' directly establishes the legality of a three-day option. The imperative indicates permission, and the hadith is a license (rukhsah) to prevent exploitation.
One might argue that the imperative indicates obligation, but here it is guidance due to the specific situation.
4
Note the grammatical refinement
The commentary discusses whether the pronoun in 'it is valid' refers to 'al-khiyar' or 'shart al-khiyar'. The preferred view is that it refers to the stipulation of the option, not the option itself, because what is stipulated is the condition.
This is a nuanced point but affects how we understand the ruling.
5
Observe the scope and refutation
The author notes that the phrase 'when you sell' in the hadith includes both seller and buyer, refuting Sufyan al-Thawri's view that only option of inspection is valid.
The hadith thus covers both parties.

سخطت فأرددها على صاحبها. وحبان بفتح الحاء المهملة والباء الموحدة والخلابة الخداع. وفائدة قوله «لا خلابة» أي لا خديعة في الدين لأن الدين النصيحة وللإعلام بأنه ليس من ذوي البصائر بالسلع فالواجب نصيحته فلا تخدعوه بشيء اعتماداً على معرفته بل انصحوه لأنه ليس عالماً بها؛ كذا في فتح الباري والآمة شجة تصيب أم الرأس وكان حبان الثغ باللام فكان يقول «لا خذابة» فقوله إذا بايعت شامل للبائع والمشتري و به اندفع المصنف عنه في الخلع حيث قال : وصح شرط الخيار لها في الخلع لا له ومن غفل عن هذا قال ما قال اهـ. وفي حاشية أبي السعود عن الحموي الأولى أن يجعل الضمير راجعاً إلى الخيار باعتبار كونه موصوفاً بالمشروطية جعلتك بالخيار في البيع الذي نعقده ثم اشترى مطلقاً لم يثبت كما في التتارخانية. وأطلقه فشمل البيع الفاسد فهو كالصحيح يثبت فيه خيار الشرط ولما كان خلاف الأصل فإذا اختلفا في اشتراطه فالقول لمن أنكره عند الإمام في ظاهر الرواية. وعند محمد: القول لمدعيه والبينة للآخر ؛ كذا في الخانية. وشمل ما إذا شرطاه وقت العقد أو ألحقاه به فلو قال أحدهما بعد البيع ولو بأيام جعلتك بالخيار ثلاثة أيام صح إجماعاً، فلو The Book of Sales, Chapter of the Option of Stipulation. It is valid for the two contracting parties or one of them [to stipulate] three days, and if more, it is not. If he ratifies within the three, it is valid, even if he sold... And it will come also. And the ninth is the option of ratification of the contract of the unauthorized person, and the tenth is the option of loss of the described quality stipulated as due by contract, such as stipulating writing, and the eleventh is the option of specification, the twelfth in resale is the option of betrayal, the thirteenth of the options is the option of payment of the price and its absence as will come in this chapter. His statement: (It is valid for the two contracting parties or one of them three days) meaning it is permissible for the seller and the buyer together or for one of them in the mentioned period. And apparently the pronoun refers to the option, and in al-Wiqaya and al-Nifaya: the stipulation of the option is valid, so he expressed it. And better is what is in al-Islah: the stipulation of the option is valid because what is described as valid is the stipulation of the option, not the option itself. And the basis for its establishment is what Ibn Majah narrated in his Sunan that Hibban ibn Munqidh was a man who had a head wound that broke his teeth, and he was not deterred from trade by that, so he was frequently cheated. He came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and mentioned that to him, so he said to him: 'When you sell, say: no cheating, then you have the option in every commodity you purchase for three nights. If you are pleased, keep it, and if you are displeased, return it to its owner.' Hibban with a fat-ha on the ha and a shadda on the ba. Al-khilaba is deception. The benefit of his saying 'no cheating' is 'no deception in religion' because religion is sincerity, and to inform that he is not a discerning person regarding goods, so it is obligatory to advise him, so do not deceive him with something relying on his knowledge, but advise him because he is not knowledgeable about them. Likewise in Fath al-Bari. Al-ammah is a wound that strikes the mother of the head. And Hibban had a lisp with the lam so he would say 'la khadhaba'. So his statement 'when you sell' includes the seller and the buyer, and with this the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri is refuted that only the option of inspection is permissible, as we presented in the issue of the pond and the buried. His statement: (And the apparent that the pronoun...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: the pronoun in 'valid' refers to the annexed (mudaf ilayh) by the context of 'valid'. And the author made it explicit in divorce (khul') where he said: and the stipulation of the option for her in khul' is valid, not for him. And whoever is heedless of this says what he said. And in the footnote of Abu al-Sa'ud from al-Hamawi: the first is to make the pronoun refer to the option in consideration of its being described as stipulated before the annexation, for the annexation of 'option' to 'stipulation' is the annexation of the described to the attribute? Actually, it is the annexation of the description? And it does not contradict their statement that it is the annexation of the ruling to its cause, and the origin is the chapter of the stipulated option, such that the infinitive is in the sense of the passive participle. This indicates that what is described as valid is not only the option as suggested by the speech of Sadr al-Shari'ah, nor only the stipulation as suggested by the speech of the author of al-Islah. His statement: (And al-khilaba...) Al-Ramli said: Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyya mentioned in Sharh al-Rawd here branches that our principles do not reject. He said: Branch: his statement (i.e., the contracting party) 'la khilaba' with a kasra on the kha is a phrase in the Shariah meaning stipulating the option of three, and its meaning is no exploitation and no deception. If they utter it while knowing, not ignorant, and not one of them ignorant, then it is valid, i.e., the option is established. And if the one for whom the option is stipulated drops the three days' option, dropping the first day invalidates the whole. He said in al-Majmu': And if he drops the option of the third, what preceded it does not drop; or the option of the second on condition that the option of the third remains, then the option of both days drops, because just as it is not permissible to stipulate a deferred option, so it is not permissible to retain a deferred option. We only drop the two days to give weight to the dropping, because the origin is the binding nature of the contract. And indeed the contract does not (for the buyer, acting on the hadith of al-Hakim, so he gave him the option in what he purchased, and because it is permitted only due to the need to repel exploitation by deliberation, and they are equal in that. And in al-Khaniyyah: if the option is stipulated for both, the ruling of the contract does not take effect at all. And his statement 'for the two contracting parties' indicates that the stipulation was after the contract or concurrent with it, to exclude the case before it. So if he said 'I make you the option in the sale we will conclude' then bought absolutely, it is not established as in al-Tatar Khaniyyah. And he gave it absolutely so it includes the invalid sale, so it is like the valid one in which the option of stipulation is established. And since it is against the original, if they dispute about its stipulation, the statement is of the one who denies it according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) in the apparent narration. And according to Muhammad, the statement is of the one who claims it, and the evidence is for the other. This is in al-Khaniyyah. And it includes if they stipulated it at the time of the contract or annexed it to it. So if one of them said after the sale, even days later, 'I make you the option for three days,' it is valid by consensus. So if they stipulated it after [the sale] for more than three, the contract is invalid according to him (Abu Hanifa) contrary to them (the two companions), just as if they annexed a corrupt condition to the sale, then it is annexed and invalidates the contract according to him, and according to them it does not invalidate and the condition is void. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: it is valid in eight [things]: sale, lease, division, settlement for specific property and unspecified, kitabah, khul', emancipation for property, from things: in sale even if stipulated for a woman or a slave. And if the option is stipulated for the mortgagor, it is valid, not for the mortgagee, because he may revoke the mortgage at any time without option. And if he guarantees with himself or property and stipulates the option for the guarantee beneficiary or the guarantor, it is valid. And stipulating the option in absolution (ibra') is valid, such as saying 'I absolve you on condition that I have the option'; mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam from the discussion of jest. And stipulating it in delivery of preemption after the request of cohabitation is also valid; mentioned by him. And stipulating it in hawalah is also valid, and in waqf according to Abu Yusuf's opinion. And its validity is probable in muzara'ah and mu'amalah because they are lease, so they are fifteen places. And it is not valid in marriage, divorce, oath, vow, acknowledgment of a contract, currency exchange, salam, and agency. Qadi Khan explained it by saying it only enters into a binding [contract] that is subject to revocation. We permitted the option of stipulation as a license, so if a defect occurs to it, the ruling is that the contract is binding. So reflect on it, you will find it agreeing with our school. And Allah knows best. His statement: (So it is like the valid one in which the option of stipulation is established) He said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: even if he sold a slave for a thousand dirhams and a pound of wine with an option, then took possession and emancipated him, it is not valid, neither executory nor suspended. His statement: (And lease) He said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if he leases with an option for him for three days, it is valid like a sale. So if he rescinds on the third, is the lessee obliged to pay the rent for two days? Al-Sattar? gave a fatwa that it is not obligatory because he was not able to benefit due to the option, because if he benefited, his option would be voided. His statement: (So they are fifteen places) Al-Nahr added another one: iqalah (rescission) where he said: in al-Bazzaziyyah, iqalah is like sale, stipulating the option therein is valid. And he added to what is not valid? He took from the later reasoning of Qadi Khan and said: by analogy, it is not valid in bequest. He organized the two categories but did not complete their count, rather he omitted from the first category kitabah, muzara'ah, and mu'amalah i.e., musaqah, and from the second category bequest. It is as if he omitted kitabah inadvertently, and the others because they are not explicitly mentioned. I have organized all, indicating the discussion in it, and I said: The option of stipulation is valid in: leaving preemption, absolution, waqf, guarantee, division, khul', emancipation, iqalah, settlement for property, then hawalah, mortgage, likewise lease, and were added musaqah and muzara'ah for them. And it is not valid in currency exchange, marriage, salam, vow, divorce, kitabah, and sale?
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in sales. The author, Ibn Nujaym, begins by affirming the basic ruling: it is valid for the two contracting parties or either one of them to stipulate a period of choice up to three days. If they stipulate more than three, the contract is invalid according to Abu Hanifa (the Imam), while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the contract remains valid and the condition is void. The passage then discusses the grammatical nuance in the matn, debating whether the pronoun refers to 'al-khiyar' (the option) or 'shart al-khiyar' (the stipulation of the option), with the preferred view being that it refers to the stipulation itself. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Majah about Hibban ibn Munqidh, who was often cheated due to a head injury. The Prophet (PBUH) instructed him to say 'la khilaba' (no cheating) and gave him a three-day option. This hadith establishes the license of khiyar al-shart for up to three days. The phrase 'la khilaba' is explained as a declaration against deception and an indication of the need to advise the ignorant buyer. The option is valid in both valid and invalid sales, as it is a license attached to the contract. If the parties dispute whether the option was stipulated, the statement of the one who denies it is accepted according to Abu Hanifa, while Muhammad says the claimant is believed. The passage also clarifies that the option can be stipulated for various contracts beyond sales, listing fifteen places: sale, lease, division, settlement, kitabah, khul', emancipation, iqalah, absolution, preemption, hawalah, mortgage, guarantee, musaqah, and muzara'ah. It is not valid in marriage, divorce, oaths, vows, acknowledgment, currency exchange, salam, and agency, because these are not subject to revocation or are non-binding. The reasoning is that khiyar al-shart is a license that only enters contracts that are inherently binding but permit revocation for a reason. The commentary ends with a note on the consequences of stipulating the option in a corrupt sale (e.g., wine), where the contract is void and emancipation does not take effect.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing one or both parties to confirm or rescind the contract within a specified period (max 3 days).
خلابة (khilaba): Deception or cheating in a transaction. The phrase 'la khilaba' is a declaration against deceit.
فسد العقد (fasada al-'aqd): The contract becomes invalid (fasid) in Hanafi terminology, meaning it is not legally effective but may require cancellation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the validity of khiyar al-shart for three days in the Hanafi school?
A) Consensus of the Companions
B) The hadith of Hibban ibn Munqidh narrated by Ibn Majah
C) Qiyas on the option of inspection
D) The practice of the people of Madinah

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart up to three days is valid (sahih) based on the Prophet's hadith; exceeding three days leads to a fasid contract according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
The Intra-Madhhab Dispute on Exceeding Three Days
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of stipulating more than three days in khiyar al-shart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn when khiyar al-shart exceeds three days and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: contract becomes fasid if option exceeds three days; Sahibayn: contract valid, condition void.

While the basic ruling of khiyar al-shart is clear, a key intra-madhhab dispute arises when the stipulated period exceeds three days. Imam Abu Hanifa takes a strict view that the contract becomes fasid (invalid), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that the contract remains valid and only the excessive condition is void. This lesson unpacks the arguments and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa holds that if the option is stipulated for more than three days, the contract becomes fasid (invalid). The condition is corrupt and invalidates the contract.
The hadith limits the option to three days, so exceeding that is an illegal condition.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the contract remains valid, but the condition (excessive option) is void. The contract is binding without any option.
They consider the condition separate; its nullity does not spread to the contract.
3
Follow each proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the option is attached to the contract in a way that its invalidity corrupts the contract. The Sahibayn analogize to other void conditions that do not invalidate the contract.
The hadith's explicit limit is the basis for Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: with a 10-day option, Abu Hanifa says the sale is null and must be re-contracted; the Sahibayn say the sale is valid immediately with no option.
This difference affects the validity of transactions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author, Ibn Nujaym, indicates that Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon (mufta bihi). The tarjih is based on the principle that licenses are restricted to their textual limits.
Later Hanafi practice follows Abu Hanifa.

صح للمتبايعين أو لأحدهما ثلاثة أيام ولو أكثر لا فإذا أجاز في الثلاث صح ولو باع
وسيأتي أيضاً. والتاسع خيار إجازة عقد الفضولي والعاشر خيار فوات الوصف المشروط المستحق بالعقد كاشتراطه الكتابة والحادي عشر خيار التعيين الثاني عشر في المرابحة خيار الخيانة. الثالث عشر من الخيارات خيار أسنانه وكان لا يدع على ذلك التجارة فكان لا يزال يغبن فأتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر له ذلك فقال له : إذا أنت بايعت فقل لا خلابة، ثم أنت في كل سلعة ابتعتها بالخيار ثلاث ليال فإذا رضيت فأمسك، وإن سخطت فأرددها على صاحبها. وحبان بفتح الحاء المهملة والباء الموحدة والخلابة الخداع. وفائدة قوله «لا خلابة» أي لا خديعة في الدين لأن الدين النصيحة وللإعلام بأنه ليس من ذوي البصائر بالسلع فالواجب نصيحته فلا تخدعوه بشيء اعتماداً على معرفته بل انصحوه لأنه ليس عالماً بها؛ كذا في فتح الباري والآمة شجة تصيب أم الرأس وكان حبان الثغ باللام فكان يقول «لا خذابة» فقوله إذا بايعت شامل للبائع والمشتري و به اندفع قول سفيان الثوري إنه لا يجوز إلا الخيار خيار كشف الحال كما قدمناه في مسألة الحفيرة والمطمورة قوله : (والظاهر أن الضمير الخ) قال في النهر أقول : الضمير في «صح» يعود إلى المضاف إليه بقرينة صح ولقد أفصح المصنف عنه في الخلع حيث قال : وصح شرط الخيار لها في الخلع لا له ومن غفل عن هذا قال ما قال اهـ. وفي حاشية أبي السعود عن الحموي الأولى أن يجعل الضمير راجعاً إلى الخيار باعتبار كونه موصوفاً بالمشروطية قبل الإضافة فإن إضافة خيار إلى الشرط من إضافة الموصوف لا الصفة، ولا ينافيه قولهم إنه من إضافة الحكم إلى سببه والأصل باب الخيار المشروط على أن يكون المصدر بمعنى اسم المفعول يدلك على ذلك أن الموصوف بالصحة ليس الخيار فقط كما يوهمه كلام صدر الشريعة، ولا الشرط فقط كما يو رهمه كلام صاحب الإصلاح قوله : (والخلابة الخ ) قال الرملي : ذكر شيخ الإسلام زكريا في شرح الروض هنا فروعاً وقواعدنا لا تأباها قال : فرع قوله - أي العاقد ـ لا خلابة بكسر الخاء • عبارة في الشرع عن اشتراط خيار الثلاث ومعناها لا غبن ولا خديعة فإن أطلقاها عالمين لا جاهلين ولا جاهل أحدهما معناها صح أي ثبت الخيار وإن أسقط من شرط له الخيار ثلاثة أيام خيار اليوم الأول بطل الكل. قال في المجموع : وإن أسقط خيار الثالث لم يسقط ما قبله أو خيار الثاني بشرط أن يبقى خيار الثالث سقط خيار اليومين جميعاً لأنه كما لا يجوز أن يشرط خياراً متراخياً عن يجوز أن يستبقي خياراً متراخياً. وإنما أسقطنا اليومين تغليباً للإسقاط لأن الأصل لزوم العقد، وإنما العقد لا للمشتري عملاً بحديث الحاكم فجعل له الخيار فيما اشتراه ولأنه إنما جاز للحاجة إلى دفع الغبن بالتروي وهما فيها سواء. وفي الخانية : إذا شرط الخيار لهما لا يثبت حكم العقد أصلاً اهـ. وقيد بقوله للمتبايعين الدال على أن الشرط كان بعد العقد أو مقارناً له للاحتراز عما إذا كان قبله، فلو قال جعلتك بالخيار في البيع الذي نعقده ثم اشترى مطلقاً لم يثبت كما في التتارخانية. وأطلقه فشمل البيع الفاسد فهو كالصحيح يثبت فيه خيار الشرط ولما كان خلاف الأصل فإذا اختلفا في اشتراطه فالقول لمن أنكره عند الإمام في ظاهر الرواية. وعند محمد: القول لمدعيه والبينة للآخر ؛ كذا في الخانية. وشمل ما إذا شرطاه وقت العقد أو ألحقاه به فلو قال أحدهما بعد البيع ولو بأيام جعلتك بالخيار ثلاثة أيام صح إجماعاً، فلو شرطاه بعده أزيد الثلاثة فسد العقد عنده خلافاً لهما كما لو ألحقا بالبيع شرطاً فاسداً فإنه يلتحق ويفسد العقد عنده، وعندهما لا يفسد ويبطل الشرط. وفي جامع الفصولين : هو يصح في ثمانية وإجارة وقسمة وصلح عن مال بعينه وبغير عينه وكتابة وخلع وعتق على مال من أشياء : في بيع شاء لو شرط للمرأة والقن. ولو شرط الخيار للراهن جاز لا للمرتهن إذ له نقض الرهن متى بلا خيار ولو كفل بنفس أو مال وشرط الخيار للمكفول له أو للكفيل جاز اهـ. ويصح شرط الخيار في الإبراء بأن قال أبرأتك على أني بالخيار ؛ ذكره فخر الإسلام من بحث الهزل. ويصح أيضاً اشتراطه في تسليم الشفعة بعد طلب المواثبة ذكره فيه أيضاً ويصح اشتراطه في الحوالة أيضاً وفي الوقف على قول أبي يوسف، وينبغي صحته في المزارعة والمعاملة لأنها إجارة فهي خمسة عشر موضعاً ولا يصح في النكاح والطلاق واليمين والنذر والإقرار بعقد والصرف والسلم والوكالة علله قاضيخان بأنه إنما يدخل في لازم يحتمل الفسخ .جوزنا خيار الشرط رخصة فإذا عرض له خلل حكم بلزوم العقد .اهـ. فتأمله تجده موافقاً لمذهبنا والله تعالى أعلم .اهـ. قوله : (فهو كالصحيح يثبت فيه خيار الشرط قال في جامع الفصولين : The Book of Sales, Chapter of the Option of Stipulation. It is valid for the two contracting parties or one of them [to stipulate] three days, and if more, it is not. If he ratifies within the three, it is valid, even if he sold... And it will come also. And the ninth is the option of ratification of the contract of the unauthorized person, and the tenth is the option of loss of the described quality stipulated as due by contract, such as stipulating writing, and the eleventh is the option of specification, the twelfth in resale is the option of betrayal, the thirteenth of the options is the option of payment of the price and its absence as will come in this chapter. His statement: (It is valid for the two contracting parties or one of them three days) meaning it is permissible for the seller and the buyer together or for one of them in the mentioned period. And apparently the pronoun refers to the option, and in al-Wiqaya and al-Nifaya: the stipulation of the option is valid, so he expressed it. And better is what is in al-Islah: the stipulation of the option is valid because what is described as valid is the stipulation of the option, not the option itself. And the basis for its establishment is what Ibn Majah narrated in his Sunan that Hibban ibn Munqidh was a man who had a head wound that broke his teeth, and he was not deterred from trade by that, so he was frequently cheated. He came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and mentioned that to him, so he said to him: 'When you sell, say: no cheating, then you have the option in every commodity you purchase for three nights. If you are pleased, keep it, and if you are displeased, return it to its owner.' Hibban with a fat-ha on the ha and a shadda on the ba. Al-khilaba is deception. The benefit of his saying 'no cheating' is 'no deception in religion' because religion is sincerity, and to inform that he is not a discerning person regarding goods, so it is obligatory to advise him, so do not deceive him with something relying on his knowledge, but advise him because he is not knowledgeable about them. Likewise in Fath al-Bari. Al-ammah is a wound that strikes the mother of the head. And Hibban had a lisp with the lam so he would say 'la khadhaba'. So his statement 'when you sell' includes the seller and the buyer, and with this the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri is refuted that only the option of inspection is permissible, as we presented in the issue of the pond and the buried. His statement: (And the apparent that the pronoun...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: the pronoun in 'valid' refers to the annexed (mudaf ilayh) by the context of 'valid'. And the author made it explicit in divorce (khul') where he said: and the stipulation of the option for her in khul' is valid, not for him. And whoever is heedless of this says what he said. And in the footnote of Abu al-Sa'ud from al-Hamawi: the first is to make the pronoun refer to the option in consideration of its being described as stipulated before the annexation, for the annexation of 'option' to 'stipulation' is the annexation of the described to the attribute? Actually, it is the annexation of the description? And it does not contradict their statement that it is the annexation of the ruling to its cause, and the origin is the chapter of the stipulated option, such that the infinitive is in the sense of the passive participle. This indicates that what is described as valid is not only the option as suggested by the speech of Sadr al-Shari'ah, nor only the stipulation as suggested by the speech of the author of al-Islah. His statement: (And al-khilaba...) Al-Ramli said: Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyya mentioned in Sharh al-Rawd here branches that our principles do not reject. He said: Branch: his statement (i.e., the contracting party) 'la khilaba' with a kasra on the kha is a phrase in the Shariah meaning stipulating the option of three, and its meaning is no exploitation and no deception. If they utter it while knowing, not ignorant, and not one of them ignorant, then it is valid, i.e., the option is established. And if the one for whom the option is stipulated drops the three days' option, dropping the first day invalidates the whole. He said in al-Majmu': And if he drops the option of the third, what preceded it does not drop; or the option of the second on condition that the option of the third remains, then the option of both days drops, because just as it is not permissible to stipulate a deferred option, so it is not permissible to retain a deferred option. We only drop the two days to give weight to the dropping, because the origin is the binding nature of the contract. And indeed the contract does not (for the buyer, acting on the hadith of al-Hakim, so he gave him the option in what he purchased, and because it is permitted only due to the need to repel exploitation by deliberation, and they are equal in that. And in al-Khaniyyah: if the option is stipulated for both, the ruling of the contract does not take effect at all. And his statement 'for the two contracting parties' indicates that the stipulation was after the contract or concurrent with it, to exclude the case before it. So if he said 'I make you the option in the sale we will conclude' then bought absolutely, it is not established as in al-Tatar Khaniyyah. And he gave it absolutely so it includes the invalid sale, so it is like the valid one in which the option of stipulation is established. And since it is against the original, if they dispute about its stipulation, the statement is of the one who denies it according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) in the apparent narration. And according to Muhammad, the statement is of the one who claims it, and the evidence is for the other. This is in al-Khaniyyah. And it includes if they stipulated it at the time of the contract or annexed it to it. So if one of them said after the sale, even days later, 'I make you the option for three days,' it is valid by consensus. So if they stipulated it after [the sale] for more than three, the contract is invalid according to him (Abu Hanifa) contrary to them (the two companions), just as if they annexed a corrupt condition to the sale, then it is annexed and invalidates the contract according to him, and according to them it does not invalidate and the condition is void. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: it is valid in eight [things]: sale, lease, division, settlement for specific property and unspecified, kitabah, khul', emancipation for property, from things: in sale even if stipulated for a woman or a slave. And if the option is stipulated for the mortgagor, it is valid, not for the mortgagee, because he may revoke the mortgage at any time without option. And if he guarantees with himself or property and stipulates the option for the guarantee beneficiary or the guarantor, it is valid. And stipulating the option in absolution (ibra') is valid, such as saying 'I absolve you on condition that I have the option'; mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam from the discussion of jest. And stipulating it in delivery of preemption after the request of cohabitation is also valid; mentioned by him. And stipulating it in hawalah is also valid, and in waqf according to Abu Yusuf's opinion. And its validity is probable in muzara'ah and mu'amalah because they are lease, so they are fifteen places. And it is not valid in marriage, divorce, oath, vow, acknowledgment of a contract, currency exchange, salam, and agency. Qadi Khan explained it by saying it only enters into a binding [contract] that is subject to revocation. We permitted the option of stipulation as a license, so if a defect occurs to it, the ruling is that the contract is binding. So reflect on it, you will find it agreeing with our school. And Allah knows best. His statement: (So it is like the valid one in which the option of stipulation is established) He said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: even if he sold a slave for a thousand dirhams and a pound of wine with an option, then took possession and emancipated him, it is not valid, neither executory nor suspended. His statement: (And lease) He said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if he leases with an option for him for three days, it is valid like a sale. So if he rescinds on the third, is the lessee obliged to pay the rent for two days? Al-Sattar? gave a fatwa that it is not obligatory because he was not able to benefit due to the option, because if he benefited, his option would be voided. His statement: (So they are fifteen places) Al-Nahr added another one: iqalah (rescission) where he said: in al-Bazzaziyyah, iqalah is like sale, stipulating the option therein is valid. And he added to what is not valid? He took from the later reasoning of Qadi Khan and said: by analogy, it is not valid in bequest. He organized the two categories but did not complete their count, rather he omitted from the first category kitabah, muzara'ah, and mu'amalah i.e., musaqah, and from the second category bequest. It is as if he omitted kitabah inadvertently, and the others because they are not explicitly mentioned. I have organized all, indicating the discussion in it, and I said: The option of stipulation is valid in: leaving preemption, absolution, waqf, guarantee, division, khul', emancipation, iqalah, settlement for property, then hawalah, mortgage, likewise lease, and were added musaqah and muzara'ah for them. And it is not valid in currency exchange, marriage, salam, vow, divorce, kitabah, and sale?
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in sales. The author, Ibn Nujaym, begins by affirming the basic ruling: it is valid for the two contracting parties or either one of them to stipulate a period of choice up to three days. If they stipulate more than three, the contract is invalid according to Abu Hanifa (the Imam), while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the contract remains valid and the condition is void. The passage then discusses the grammatical nuance in the matn, debating whether the pronoun refers to 'al-khiyar' (the option) or 'shart al-khiyar' (the stipulation of the option), with the preferred view being that it refers to the stipulation itself. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Majah about Hibban ibn Munqidh, who was often cheated due to a head injury. The Prophet (PBUH) instructed him to say 'la khilaba' (no cheating) and gave him a three-day option. This hadith establishes the license of khiyar al-shart for up to three days. The phrase 'la khilaba' is explained as a declaration against deception and an indication of the need to advise the ignorant buyer. The option is valid in both valid and invalid sales, as it is a license attached to the contract. If the parties dispute whether the option was stipulated, the statement of the one who denies it is accepted according to Abu Hanifa, while Muhammad says the claimant is believed. The passage also clarifies that the option can be stipulated for various contracts beyond sales, listing fifteen places: sale, lease, division, settlement, kitabah, khul', emancipation, iqalah, absolution, preemption, hawalah, mortgage, guarantee, musaqah, and muzara'ah. It is not valid in marriage, divorce, oaths, vows, acknowledgment, currency exchange, salam, and agency, because these are not subject to revocation or are non-binding. The reasoning is that khiyar al-shart is a license that only enters contracts that are inherently binding but permit revocation for a reason. The commentary ends with a note on the consequences of stipulating the option in a corrupt sale (e.g., wine), where the contract is void and emancipation does not take effect.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing one or both parties to confirm or rescind the contract within a specified period (max 3 days).
فسد العقد (fasada al-'aqd): The contract becomes invalid (fasid) in Hanafi terminology, meaning it is not legally effective but may require cancellation.
الثلاثة أيام (al-thalathat ayyam): The maximum period for khiyar al-shart, fixed at three days based on the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what happens if a seller and buyer stipulate a 10-day option in a sale?
A) The contract is valid and the option is effective for 10 days.
B) The contract is fasid and must be re-contracted without the excessive condition.
C) The contract is valid but the option is reduced to 3 days.
D) The contract is batil (void) and no rights arise.

Key Takeaway
When khiyar al-shart exceeds three days, the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the contract becomes fasid (invalid) and must be annulled.

Khiyar al-Shart: Ruling, Proof, and the Burden of Proof Dispute
States the ruling, proof, conditions, and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of khiyar al-shart, identify its hadith proof, list the conditions for its validity, and explain why Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad differ on the burden of proof when its stipulation is disputed.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart suspends finality for three days; if disputed, the denier is believed (Abu Hanifa) unless evidence is provided.

This lesson examines the basic ruling of Khiyar al-Shart (Option of Stipulation) — its permissibility, proof from the hadith of al-Hakim, and the key condition that the stipulation must occur at or after the contract. It also delves into an important intra-Hanafi procedural dispute: when the parties disagree about whether the option was stipulated, whose word is accepted? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply procedural maxims in fiqh and appreciate the nuance within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify that the act under discussion is khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) and that it is permissible (ja'iz) for both parties based on the hadith of al-Hakim.
The ruling is not fard or wajib; it is a permissible right that can be included in a contract.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'You have the option in every sale for three days' (al-Hakim). This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut and dalala are both zanni.
The hadith is not mutawatir, thus it provides a zanni proof, sufficient for a permissive ruling.
3
Identify the conditions
The stipulation must be made at the time of the contract or after it, not before. A pre-contract promise does not create a valid khiyar.
The condition is deduced from the phrase 'for the two parties' which implies contemporaneity.
4
Analyze the procedural dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that when parties dispute whether khiyar was stipulated, the denier (who denies the stipulation) is believed without evidence. Imam Muhammad holds that the claimant is believed, and the denier must provide evidence.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa's view is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the sale is deemed without option unless the claimant brings proof; under Muhammad, the sale is deemed with option unless the denier brings proof. This affects the finality of the contract.
The ruling on evidence can overturn the presumption; if evidence is provided, the dispute is resolved accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط للمشتري عملاً بحديث الحاكم فجعل له الخيار فيما اشتراه ولأنه إنما جاز للحاجة إلى دفع الغبن بالتروي وهما فيها سواء. وفي الخانية : إذا شرط الخيار لهما لا يثبت حكم العقد أصلاً اهـ. وقيد بقوله للمتبايعين الدال على أن الشرط كان بعد العقد أو مقارناً له للاحتراز عما إذا كان قبله، فلو قال جعلتك بالخيار في البيع الذي نعقده ثم اشترى مطلقاً لم يثبت كما في التتارخانية. وأطلقه فشمل البيع الفاسد فهو كالصحيح يثبت فيه خيار الشرط ولما كان خلاف الأصل فإذا اختلفا في اشتراطه فالقول لمن أنكره عند الإمام في ظاهر الرواية. وعند محمد: القول لمدعيه والبينة للآخر ؛ كذا في الخانية.
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option of Stipulation. For the buyer, acting upon the hadith of al-Hakim, so He [the Prophet] gave him the option in what he bought, and because it is only permitted due to the need to prevent harm through deliberation, and both are equal in that. In al-Khaniyah: If they stipulate the option for both, the ruling of the contract is not established at all. It is restricted by His statement 'for the two parties' indicating that the stipulation was after the contract or concurrent with it, to exclude the case when it was before. So if he said 'I make you the option in the sale we will conduct' then he bought absolutely, it is not established as in al-Tatar Khaniyah. And he made it absolute so it includes a fasid sale, so it is like a valid sale in that khiyar al-shart is established in it. And since it is contrary to the principle, if they dispute about its stipulation, the word is of the one who denies it according to Imam in the apparent narration. And according to Muhammad: the word is of the claimant and the evidence is for the other; as in al-Khaniyah.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on Khiyar al-Shart (Option of Stipulation). It first states the ruling: the buyer has the right to stipulate a period of option in the sale, based on the hadith of al-Hakim (meaning the hadith: 'You have the option in every sale for three days' as narrated by al-Hakim and others). The reason for its permissibility is the need to protect against deception (ghabn) by allowing time for deliberation; both buyer and seller are equal in this need. The passage then references al-Khaniyah: if both parties stipulate option for themselves, the contract does not become binding at all. The condition is that the stipulation must be at or after the contract, not before. A pre-contractual promise of option does not create a valid khiyar. The ruling applies even to a fasid (defective) sale, meaning khiyar al-shart is established in it just as in a valid sale. Finally, since granting option is an exception to the principle that a sale is binding immediately, if the parties dispute whether it was stipulated, the word of the denier is taken according to Imam Abu Hanifa (in Zahir al-Riwayah), while Muhammad al-Shaybani says the claimant's word is taken with the requirement of evidence. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on procedural law.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by one or both parties in a contract, allowing them to rescind within a specified period (usually three days).
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A sale that is defective due to an illegality in its subject matter or price but can be corrected; it is not null and void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa (Zahir al-Riwayah), if the buyer and seller disagree about whether a khiyar al-shart was stipulated, whose word is taken?
A) The word of the person who claims the stipulation.
B) The word of the person who denies it.
C) The word of the person with witnesses.
D) The word of the buyer always.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is a permissible option that suspends the binding nature of a sale for up to three days; when its stipulation is disputed, the Hanafi mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa) is that the denier is believed without evidence.

Khiyar After Contract: The Three-Day Consensus and the Dispute on Exceeding
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar stipulated after contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on stipulating khiyar al-shart after the contract and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding khiyar exceeding three days.

Core Idea
Stipulating khiyar after the contract is valid by consensus for three days; exceeding it divides the school.

This passage examines a specific scenario: the stipulation of khiyar al-shart after the contract has been concluded. While both the Imam and his two disciples agree on the validity of a three-day option even if stipulated later, they differ when the period exceeds three days. Understanding this dispute reveals deeper principles about the effect of invalid conditions on contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed-upon ruling
Note that stipulating a three-day option after the contract is valid by consensus. The passage begins with this: 'if one of them says after the sale, I grant you the option for three days, it is valid by consensus.'
This consensus covers both stipulation at contract and after.
2
Pinpoint the point of dispute
The ikhtilaf arises when the stipulated period exceeds three days. Abu Hanifa says the sale becomes fasid; the Sahibayn say the sale remains valid and the condition is void.
3
Analyze the Imam's reasoning (qiyas)
Abu Hanifa analogizes to a fasid condition inserted at the time of contract: just as that corrupts the sale, so does attaching a fasid condition after the contract. The 'illa' is the attachment of an impermissible condition.
He treats the attachment as equivalent to insertion.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn distinguish: a condition added after the contract is extrinsic and does not affect the contract's validity. The sale is complete; only the condition itself is void.
They limit the effect of the condition to the agreement itself.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the sale is fasid, the goods must be returned; if valid with a void condition, the sale stands and the buyer has no option. This directly impacts the parties' obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل ما إذا شرطاه وقت العقد أو ألحقاه به فلو قال أحدهما بعد البيع ولو بأيام جعلتك بالخيار ثلاثة أيام صح إجماعاً، فلو شرطاه بعده أزيد الثلاثة فسد العقد عنده خلافاً لهما كما لو ألحقا بالبيع شرطاً فاسداً فإنه يلتحق ويفسد العقد عنده، وعندهما لا يفسد ويبطل الشرط.
And it includes the case when they stipulate it at the time of the contract or attach it to it. So if one of them says after the sale, even after days, 'I make you the option for three days', it is valid by consensus. If they stipulate it afterwards exceeding three days, the contract is fasid according to him [Abu Hanifa], contrary to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], just as if they attach a fasid condition to the sale, then it attaches and makes the contract fasid according to him, while according to them it does not make it fasid and the condition is void.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the timing of the stipulation. It states that if khiyar is stipulated at the time of the contract or attached to it (i.e., after the contract but still in the same session), the ruling applies. Specifically, if after the sale one party says, 'I grant you the option for three days', even if days have passed since the sale, it is valid by consensus (as long as it is within the option period? Actually the text says 'after the sale even after days' which seems to mean after the transaction, even if a few days have passed, the stipulation is valid by consensus up to three days. However, if they stipulate a period longer than three days after the contract, Imam Abu Hanifa says the sale becomes fasid, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the sale remains valid and the condition is void. Their analogy: if a fasid condition is attached to a sale, Imam says it makes the sale fasid, but they say it does not; the condition is merely void. This is a direct application of the earlier ruling on inserting a fasid condition. The word 'عنده' refers to Abu Hanifa, 'عندهما' to the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
ألحقاه به (alhaqahu bihi): Attached it to the contract, meaning the option was stipulated after the contract but considered part of the same transaction.
أزيد الثلاثة (azida al-thalatha): More than three days; the default maximum period for khiyar al-shart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is valid and the option is valid for five days.
B) The sale is fasid (corrupted).
C) The sale is void (batil).
D) The option is valid for three days only, and the sale remains valid.

Key Takeaway
The dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on exceeding three days hinges on whether a condition stipulated after the contract is treated as part of the contract or as an external agreement.

Contracts Where Khiyar al-Shart is Valid in Hanafi Fiqh
Enumerates and comments on the contracts where khiyar al-shart is valid, with additions and the reasoning of Qadikhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the fifteen contracts where khiyar al-shart is valid according to Jami' al-Fusulayn and identify the contracts where it is invalid, applying Qadikhan's reasoning.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart applies only to binding contracts that are open to rescission.

Khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) is a concession (rukhsah) in Hanafi fiqh that allows a party to rescind a contract within a specified period. Its validity is not universal; it is only permitted in certain types of contracts. This lesson will walk you through the authoritative list from Jami' al-Fusulayn and later additions, together with the underlying principle articulated by Qadikhan.

Guided Path
1
Understand the core principle
Qadikhan states: 'It only enters into a binding contract that is subject to rescission.' This is the key criterion for determining whether khiyar al-shart can be valid.
2
Identify the first list from Jami' al-Fusulayn
The passage begins with eight unspecified contracts (probably the first eight listed later: ijarah, qismah, sulh, kitabah, khul', 'itq, rahn, kafalah) and then names others. Focus on the enumeration: ijarah, qismah, sulh, kitabah, khul', 'itq bi mal, rahn (for rahin), kafalah (with self or property).
The eight are not listed explicitly, but the text says 'in eight' then proceeds to name them.
3
Note the additions to reach fifteen
Later sources add ibra' (exoneration), shuf'a (preemption), hawala (transfer of debt), waqf (according to Abu Yusuf), muzara'ah and mu'amalah (as types of ijarah), and iqalah (mutual rescission). These additions bring the count to fifteen.
Al-Nahr adds iqalah; the poem at the end organizes all.
4
Distinguish invalid contracts and apply the principle
Contracts where khiyar is not valid include: nikah, talaq, yamin, nadhr, iqrar (with a contract), sarf, salam, wakalah. Apply Qadikhan's reasoning: these are either not binding (like yamin, nadhr) or not subject to rescission (like nikah, talaq).
Wasiyya is also invalid according to qiyas, though not explicitly stated in the initial list.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: It is valid in eight [contracts] and ijarah, qismah, sulh upon specific and unspecific wealth, kitabah, khul', and 'itq against wealth. Commentary
This extensive passage enumerates the contracts in which khiyar al-shart is valid, based on Jami' al-Fusulayn and other sources. It begins by stating that it is valid in eight unspecified contracts, then lists ijarah, qismah, sulh (over specific or unspecified wealth), kitabah, khul', 'itq against payment, and then adds specific cases: for the mortgagor (rahin) but not mortgagee, for kafalah with self or property, ibra' (exoneration), shuf'a (preemption) after the first demand, hawala, waqf (according to Abu Yusuf), and likely muzara'ah and mu'amalah (because they are considered ijarah). This totals fifteen places. Then it lists contracts where khiyar is NOT valid: nikah, talaq, yamin, nadhr, iqrar (when combined with a contract), sarf, salam, and wakalah. Qadikhan's reasoning: khiyar al-shart is a concession that can only apply to contracts that are binding but subject to rescission; if a defect occurs that invalidates the concession, the contract reverts to being binding. The passage then comments on previous statements: (1) It confirms that khiyar is established even in a fasid sale, giving the example of a sale involving wine – such a sale is so corrupt that even if the slave is freed by the buyer, the freeing does not take effect. (2) In ijarah with option, if the hirer cancels on the third day, he does not owe rent for the days of option because he refrained from using the property to preserve his option. (3) The count of fifteen places is expanded by al-Nahr to include iqalah (mutual rescission) – it is like a sale. Then a poem is presented that lists all the valid contracts in a rhyming form, mentioning some omitted from earlier lists.

Key Terms
جامع الفصولين (Jami' al-Fusulayn): A Hanafi fiqh work by Ibn al-Sa'ati, compiling rulings into two parts (usul and furu').
خمسة عشر موضعاً (khamsata 'ashara mawdi'an): Fifteen places (contracts) where khiyar al-shart is valid, as listed in Jami' al-Fusulayn with additions.
لازم يحتمل الفسخ (lazim yah'tamil al-faskh): Binding contract that is subject to rescission – the condition for the validity of khiyar al-shart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following contracts is khiyar al-shart NOT valid?
A) Ijarah
B) Salam
C) Khul'
D) Hawala

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is valid only in binding contracts that are open to rescission, with a specific list of fifteen contracts in Hanafi fiqh.
