Khiyar al-Shart Time Limits and the Default to Khiyar al-Majlis
Rulings on khiyar wording and time limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish khiyar al-majlis from khiyar al-shart, apply the ruling on time limits expressed with 'ila', and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on its interpretation.

Core Idea
When 'you have the option' is said without time, it's khiyar al-majlis; with a duration, it's khiyar al-shart — and 'until' triggers a classic Hanafi ikhtilaf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq and Fath al-Qadir clarifies two critical points: first, that the mere phrase 'you have the option' defaults to khiyar al-majlis, not a lengthy khiyar al-shart; second, when a time limit is expressed with 'ila' (until), the exact endpoint is disputed between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Understanding these nuances is essential for drafting valid contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
When no time is mentioned, the phrase 'anta bi al-khiyar' gives only khiyar al-majlis, not a long option period.
This is a key distinction: the default is the session option.
2
Recognize khiyar al-shart
When a duration is specified (e.g., 'until noon'), it becomes khiyar al-shart with a fixed period.
The specificity of the time converts the option to khiyar al-shart.
3
Analyze the 'ila' dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that 'ila' includes the endpoint; Sahibayn hold it excludes the endpoint. This affects when the option expires.
Example: 'until noon' – Abu Hanifa says option lasts until the end of noon time; Sahibayn say until the beginning of noon.
4
Apply the dispute to a practical case
If the buyer cancels after noon but before asr, according to Abu Hanifa it is valid; according to Sahibayn, the option has expired.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is a real difference in rulings.
5
Note the extension to other phrases and part-option
The same principle applies to 'until night' or 'until three days'. Also, the option can be stipulated in part of the goods (half, third, quarter) and is valid.
These rules are derived from al-Ziyadat and al-Sirajiyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باشتراط الخيار العقد يوم من رمضان ويومين وفي الولوالجية : اشترى عبداً واشترط أن للمشتري خيار يومين بعد شهر رمضان والشراء في آخر رمضان فهو جائز ويكون له الخيار ثلاثة أيام اليوم بعده لأنه سكت عن الخيار يوم العقد وأمكن تصحيح هذا العقد، ولعل تصحيح هذا العقد ويومين بعد رمضان ولو قال البائع للمشتري لا خيار لك في رمضان فالبيع فاسد لأنه تعذر تصحيح العقد اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: لو قال له أنت بالخيار فله خيار المجلس فقط، ولو قال إلى الظهر فعند أبي حنيفة يستمر إلى أن يخرج وقت الظهر، وعندهما لا تدخل الغاية .اهـ وكذا إلى الليل أو إلى ثلاثة أيام يدخل ما بعد إلى. وشمل ما إذا شرطاه في كل المبيع أو بعضه لما في السراجية: اشترى مكيلاً أو موزوناً أو عبداً وشرط الخيار له في نصفه أو ثلثه أو ربعه جاز مذكورة في الزيادات .اهـ. وسيأتي حكم ما إذا كان المبيع متعدداً فجعل الخيار في البعض وهو خيار التعيين.
With the stipulation of option in the contract [on a particular day?], one day from Ramadan and two days. And in al-Walwaljiyya: He bought a slave and stipulated that the buyer has an option of two days after the month of Ramadan, and the purchase was at the end of Ramadan, so it is permissible and he has an option of three days: the day after (i.e., the first of Shawwal?) because he remained silent about the option on the day of contract, and it is possible to correct this contract, and it is possible to correct it as two days after Ramadan. And if the seller said to the buyer, 'You have no option in Ramadan,' the sale is fasid because it is impossible to correct the contract. In Fath al-Qadir: If he said to him 'You have the option' he has only khiyar al-majlis. And if he said 'until noon,' then according to Abu Hanifa it continues until the time of noon departs (i.e., afternoon begins), and according to them (the Sahibayn) the extent (nihaayah) does not enter. Similarly, 'until night' or 'until three days' includes what is after 'until'. And it includes when they stipulate it in the entire sale or part of it, as in al-Sirajiyya: He bought a weighed or measured item or a slave and stipulated option in half, a third, or a quarter, it is valid; mentioned in al-Ziyadat. And the ruling when the sold item is multiple and he makes the option in part of it will come later – that is khiyar al-ta'yin.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage covers several sub-rulings of khiyar al-shart when tied to specific times. First, a case from al-Walwaljiyya: a slave is bought at the end of Ramadan, and the buyer stipulates an option of two days after Ramadan. Since the purchase occurs during Ramadan, the day of the contract is not counted in the option (the buyer is silent about option on that day). So the total option period becomes three days: the day after (Eid?), and the two days after Ramadan. If the seller says 'no option in Ramadan', the sale becomes fasid because it is impossible to validate – the option period would be zero. Next, from Fath al-Qadir: the phrase 'You have the option' is ambiguous: if said absolutely, it grants khiyar al-majlis (option of the session) only. If said 'until noon', there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa says the option lasts until the expiration of the noon time (i.e., until asr?), while the Sahibayn say the option is only until the arrival of noon, not including the time after. Similarly for 'until night' or 'until three days' – the word 'ila' (until) includes the endpoint according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn say it does not. Finally, the option can be stipulated in part of the goods (half, third, quarter) and it is valid, as mentioned in al-Ziyadat. The case of multiple items with option in one of them is called khiyar al-ta'yin and will be discussed later.

Key Terms
خيار المجلس (khiyar al-majlis): The option during the session of the contract; both parties may rescind as long as they have not separated.
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option to choose one or more items from a group when the sale includes multiple items.
إلى (ila): Preposition meaning 'until' or 'up to'; its interpretation in khiyar time limits is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the seller says to the buyer, 'You have the option until noon,' according to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does the option period end?
A) At the beginning of noon.
B) When the time of noon expires (i.e., start of asr).
C) At the end of the day.
D) After three days.

Key Takeaway
Understanding the default (khiyar al-majlis) and the linguistic rules for time limits (ila dispute) is essential for correctly drafting khiyar al-shart clauses.

Khiyar in Sarf: The Currency Exchange Dispute
Rulings on khiyar in price/goods and the sarf dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar in a sarf contract and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Khiyar in a sale does not automatically void a separate sarf contract; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ on contingency.

This lesson examines a case where a buyer stipulates khiyar in a sale and pays in a different currency (sarf). When the sale is cancelled, the validity of the currency exchange becomes disputed within the Hanafi school. Understanding this dispute illuminates the principle of contingency in subsidiary contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling context
Locate the specific transaction: a slave sold for 1000 dirhams with khiyar for the buyer, who pays 100 dinars instead. Note that the sale and the sarf are separate but linked.
The sarf is the exchange of dirhams for dinars at the time of payment.
2
State the two positions
Abu Yusuf holds that the sarf is valid despite cancellation; Abu Hanifa holds it is void. Articulate each position clearly.
Use the pronouns from the text: 'عند أبي حنيفة' and 'عن أبي يوسف'.
3
Identify the underlying reason (illah)
What is the basis for each ruling? Abu Hanifa views the sarf as contingent on the sale; Abu Yusuf views it as independent. Recognize the qiyas.
Think of khiyar as making the sale conditional; does that condition affect the exchange?
4
Apply the dispute to a new scenario
Consider a buyer who cancels after the sarf. Determine the consequences under each position: what must be returned?
Under Abu Yusuf: dinars stay, dirhams returned; under Abu Hanifa: both must revert.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: in real life, which ruling leads to a fairer outcome? Why might later Hanafi practice prefer Abu Yusuf?
Consider ease of transaction: if the exchange already happened, reversing it may be burdensome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتارخانية : وإذا اشترطه المشتري له في الثمن أو في المبيع كان له الخيار فيهما .اهـ. ولو اشترى عبداً بألف درهم على أن المشتري بالخيار فأعطاه بها مائة دينار ثم فسخ البيع ؛ فعن أبي يوسف الصرف جائز ويرد الدراهم والصرف باطل على قول أبي حنيفة ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. فإن قلت : قد فيه أنه صرح لو أطلق الخيار فسد البيع ولا شك أن قوله أنت بالخيار أو لك الخيار» إطلاق فما التوفيق؟ قلت : قد صور في الولوالجية والخلاصة مسألة أنت بالخيار أنه باع بلا خيار ثم لقيه بعد مدة فقال له أنت بالخيار فله الخيار ما دام في المجلس بمنزلة قوله لك الإقالة بخلاف ما إذا أطلقاه وقت العقد. وفي الخانية : ابتداء التأجيل في البيع بثمن مؤجل بخيار من وقت سقوطه لا وقت العقد، سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري، وللشفيع الطلب وقت العقد حيث علم لا وقت السقوط ويطلب في بيع الفضولي وقت الإجازة وفي البيع الفاسد حين انقطاع الاسترداد، وفي الهبة بشرط العوض روايتان في رواية يطلب عنه القبض، وفي رواية عند العقد وهو الصحيح. ولو كان الخيار للبائع فصالحه المشتري على معين لإمضاء البيع صح ويكون زيادة في الثمن، وكذا لو كان الخيار للمشتري فصالحه البائع على إسقاطه فحط عنه من الثمن كذا أو زاده عرضاً جاز ،اهـ، فلو صالحه البائع على إبطال البيع ويعطيه مائة ففعل انفسخ البيع ولا شيء له ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وأطلق في المتبايعين فشمل الأصيل والنائب فصح للوكيل والوصي كما في الخانية. ولو أمره ببيع مطلق فعقد بخيار له أو للآمر أو لأجنبي صححاه، ولو أمره ببيع بخيار للآمر فشرط لنفسه لا يجوز وإن كان اشتراط الخيار لنفسه اشتراطاً للآمر لأن الأمر إذا أمره ببيع لا يكون للمأمور فيه رأي وتدبير ويكون للآمر كله وفيما فعله يكون له رأي ويكون للآمر بطريق التبعية فيكون مخالفاً. ولو أمره بشراء بخيار من وكالة. كذلك إقرار وزيد وصية كما مر بحثاً فاغتنم ذي المقالة. قوله : (علله قاضيخان الخ) لينظر
And in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: If the buyer stipulates the option for himself in the price or in the goods, he has the option in both. And if he bought a slave for a thousand dirhams on condition that the buyer has the option, and he gave instead a hundred dinars, then cancelled the sale; according to Abu Yusuf the sarf (exchange) is valid and the dirhams are returned, while the sarf is void according to Abu Hanifa; as in al-Tatar Khaniyyah. If you say: It has been stated that if he releases the option (absolutely) the sale is corrupt, and there is no doubt that his statement 'You have the option' or 'You have the choice' is an absolute (release), so what is the reconciliation? I say: It is depicted in al-Walwaljiyya and al-Khulasa the issue of 'You have the option' that he sold without option, then after a while he met him and said 'You have the option', so he has the option as long as he is in the session, like his statement 'I give you the cancellation' (iqala), contrary to when they release it at the time of the contract. And in al-Khaniyyah: The start of the deferment in a sale with deferred price and option is from the time the option falls, not from the time of contract, whether the option is for the seller or the buyer. And the pre-emptor (shafi') makes his demand at the time of contract if he knows, not at the time the option falls. And in the sale of a fuduli (unauthorized agent), demand is at the time of ratification, and in a fasid sale, at the time of cessation of the right to reclaim. And in a gift with consideration (hiba bi shart al-'iwad), there are two narrations: in one narration, demand is upon possession; in another, at the time of contract, and that is the correct one. And if the option was for the seller, and the buyer settles with him on a specific amount to execute the sale, it is valid and constitutes an increase in the price. Likewise, if the option was for the buyer, and the seller settles with him to drop it (the option) by reducing the price or increasing a commodity, it is valid. If the seller settles with him to invalidate the sale and gives him a hundred, and he does, the sale is rescinded and he (the seller) gets nothing; as in al-Tatar Khaniyyah. And he made it absolute regarding the two parties, so it includes the principal and the agent, so it is valid for the agent and the executor as in al-Khaniyyah. And if he ordered him to sell absolutely, and he made a contract with option for himself, or for the principal, or for a third party, they (the two imams?) validate it. And if he ordered him to sell with option for the principal, and he stipulated it for himself, it is not permissible, even if stipulating the option for himself is (like) stipulating for the principal, because if he ordered him to sell, the agent has no independent opinion and management, and everything is for the principal; and in what he did, he has an opinion and it is for the principal as a subsidiary, so it is in opposition. And if he ordered him to buy with option, from agency. Likewise iqrar, and added wasiyya as passed in research, so take advantage of this article. His statement: (Qadikhan's reasoning...) to be considered.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This extensive passage covers multiple sub-rulings. First, from al-Tatar Khaniyyah: if the buyer stipulates option in the price (e.g., to pay in installments with option) or in the goods, he has option in both. Then a case of sarf (currency exchange): if the buyer buys a slave for 1000 dirhams with option, and gives 100 dinars instead, then cancels the sale, Abu Yusuf says the exchange (sarf contract) is valid (the dinars are given as payment) and the dirhams are returned (since the sale is cancelled), while Abu Hanifa says the exchange is void because the basis is invalid. This is an intra-Hanafi difference. Next, a question is raised: earlier it was stated that if the option is released absolutely ('You have the option'), the sale becomes corrupt (fasid). But here it seems that saying 'You have the option' is an absolute release. The answer: the absolute release that corrupts the sale occurs only when it is said at the time of the contract as part of the contract. If it is said after the contract, it is treated as an offer of iqalah (mutual rescission), giving the option of the session, not khiyar al-shart. Then a ruling from al-Khaniyyah: in a sale with deferred price and option, the period of deferment begins when the option ends, not from the date of contract. This applies to khiyar for either party. The pre-emptor (shafi') makes his demand at the time of the contract, not when the option ends. For a fuduli (unauthorized agent) sale, demand is at ratification; for a fasid sale, when the right to reclaim ceases. For a gift with consideration (hiba bi shart al-'iwad), there are two opinions: demand at possession or at contract, with the latter being correct. Then a ruling: if the seller has the option, and the buyer agrees to pay a specific amount to execute the sale, it is valid and the amount is an increase in price. If the buyer has the option, and the seller agrees to reduce the price to drop the option, it is valid. If the seller agrees to cancel the sale and pay the buyer 100, and he does, the sale is rescinded and the seller gets nothing (the payment is considered a penalty? Not specified). Next, agency: the rulings on khiyar apply to agents (wakil) and executors (wasi) as well. If the principal orders an agent to sell absolutely without any stipulation, and the agent makes a contract with option for himself, the principal, or a third party, it is valid (they – meaning Abu Yusuf and Muhammad – validate it). But if the principal orders him to sell with option for the principal, and the agent stipulates it for himself, it is not permissible, because the agent has no independent authority in a matter the principal has specifically directed. The agent's action is considered opposition to the principal's instruction. Finally, a brief mention of iqrar (acknowledgment) and wasiyya (bequest) in this context, and a reference to Qadikhan's reasoning.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Currency exchange; a contract for exchanging different currencies.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option stipulated by one or both parties to confirm or cancel the sale within a specified period.
إقالة (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a contract by agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The sarf is valid and the dirhams are returned.
C) The sarf is valid only if the option is for the buyer.

Key Takeaway
In khiyar cases involving sarf, the validity of the exchange is disputed; the mufta bihi often follows Abu Yusuf for practical ease.

The Three-Day Limit for Khiyar al-Shart: Abu Hanifa vs the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart, explain the evidence of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the relied-upon ruling (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
The option period is limited to three days; exceeding it invalidates the sale per Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: how long can a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart) last? Abu Hanifa restricts it to three days, while the Sahibayn permit any specified period. The commentator evaluates each proof and settles on Abu Hanifa's view. We will analyze the arguments and understand the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
State Abu Hanifa's position (invalid if >3 days) and the Sahibayn's position (valid if period is known).
Note that both agree on the validity of a three-day option; the dispute is over longer periods.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
They cite the hadith of Ibn Umar allowing a two-month option. Note that the commentator questions its authenticity and applicability.
The commentator argues the hadith is not well-known (ghayr maruf) and could refer to other options.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
He argues that the option contradicts the binding nature of the contract and is only allowed for deliberation, which three days suffice. He cites the hadith of a four-day option being invalidated.
The hadith from Abd al-Razzaq directly supports invalidity for more than three days.
4
Evaluate the response
The commentator rejects the Sahibayn's hadith as unknown and ambiguous, strengthening Abu Hanifa's view.
Also, the commentator adds that if the option is perpetual, absolute, or unknown, the sale is invalid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, as it is the majority view and supported by the commentator.
Thus, in fatwa, stipulating more than three days renders the sale fasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو أكثر (لا أي لا يصح اشتراطه أكثر من ثلاثة أيام عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يجوز إذا سمى مدة معلومة لحديث ابن عمر أنه عليه السلام أجاز الخيار إلى شهرين. وله أنه مخالف لمقتضى العقد وهو اللزوم ثبت نصاً على خلاف القياس في المدة المذكورة للتروي وهو يحصل فيها فلا حاجة إلى ما زاد عليها ويدل عليه حديث عبد الرزاق أن رجلاً اشترى من رجل بعيراً وشرط عليه الخيار أربعة أيام فأبطل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم البيع. وأما حديث ابن عمر فلم يعرف ولأنه جزء الدعوى لأنها جوازه أكثر من ثلاثة أيام طالت المدة أو قصرت، وهو يقيد بمدة خاصة، ولأنه يحتمل خيار الشرط وخيار الرؤية والعيب فلا يكون حجة وإطلاق المدة عنده كاشتراط الأكثر في عدم الجواز وإفساد البيع. ولو قال المؤلف ولو أكثر أو مؤبداً أو مطلقاً أو موقتاً بوقت مجهول لكان أولى لأن البيع فاسد في هذه كلها كما في التتارخانية . وهكذا إذا كان المبيع مما لا يتسارع إليه الفساد، فإن كان مما يتسارع فحكمه في الخانية قال : اشترى شيئاً يتسارع إليه الفساد على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فالقياس لا يجبر المشتري على شيء. وفي الاستحسان يقال للمشتري إما أن تفسخ البيع وإما أن تأخذ المبيع ولا شيء عليك من الثمن حتى تجيز البيع أو يفسد المبيع عندك دفعاً للضرر من الجانبين
His saying: (and if more) no, meaning it is not valid to stipulate more than three days according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is permissible if he specifies a known period, due to the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted the option up to two months. And for him (Abu Hanifa) it is that it contradicts the requirement of the contract, which is binding; it has been textually established contrary to analogy for the mentioned period for deliberation, and that is achieved within it, so there is no need for more than it. And it is supported by the hadith of Abd al-Razzaq that a man bought a camel from another and stipulated the option for four days, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) invalidated the sale. As for the hadith of Ibn Umar, it is not known; and because it is part of the claim: its permissibility for more than three days, whether the period is long or short, and it restricts to a specific period; and because it could be interpreted as option of stipulation, option of sight, or option of defect, so it is not authoritative. And absolute duration according to him is like stipulating the maximum in terms of non-permissibility and invalidating the sale. And if the author had said 'and if more, or perpetual, or absolute, or timed with an unknown time' it would have been better, because the sale is invalid in all these as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And similarly if the sold item is not subject to rapid decay; if it is subject to rapid decay, its ruling in al-Khaniyya: he said: he bought something that decays rapidly with the option for three days; by analogy, the buyer is not compelled to anything. And by istihsan, the buyer is told: either rescind the sale or take the item and you owe nothing of the price until you confirm the sale or the item perishes with you, to prevent harm on both sides.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart (stipulated option) in a sale. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states 'and if more' (meaning more than three days), and the commentator explains the ruling. According to Abu Hanifa, stipulating an option period longer than three days is invalid and renders the sale fasid (void). His evidence includes: the sale contract is fundamentally binding (luzum), and the option was legislated as an exception to the general rule only for the purpose of deliberation (tarawwi), which is sufficiently achieved within three days. He also cites the hadith of Abd al-Razzaq where the Prophet invalidated a sale with a four-day option. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, permitting any specified duration based on the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet allowed an option up to two months. The commentator responds that this hadith is not well-known (ghayr maruf) and also that it could apply to other types of options, not necessarily khiyar al-shart. The commentator then adds that if the author had included cases of perpetual, absolute, or unknown time, it would have been clearer; all these invalidate the sale. Finally, he discusses a subsidiary ruling: if the sold item is perishable and the option is three days, by qiyas the buyer is not compelled, but by istihsan (juristic preference) the buyer is given a choice to either rescind or take the item without paying until the sale is confirmed or the item perishes, to prevent loss.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option in a sale contract allowing one or both parties to cancel the sale within a specified period.
ترو (tarawwi): Deliberation; the purpose of khiyar al-shart is to give time for the buyer or seller to reflect on the transaction.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that overrides strict analogy to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the maximum permissible period for khiyar al-shart?
A) As agreed by the parties
B) Three days
C) One month
D) Two months

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's three-day limit for khiyar al-shart is the relied-upon Hanafi position, based on the purpose of deliberation and supporting hadith.

Istihsan Overrides Qiyas When Goods Are Perishable
Subsidiary ruling on perishable goods with khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the qiyas and istihsan rulings when a perishable item is sold with a three-day option, and apply the istihsan ruling.

Core Idea
For perishable goods, istihsan gives the buyer a choice to protect against loss.

This part of the passage addresses an edge case: what if the sold item is perishable (e.g., fruits or vegetables) and the buyer has a three-day option? By strict qiyas, the buyer is not compelled to do anything, but the scholar adopts istihsan, allowing the buyer either to rescind or take the item without immediate payment, to prevent loss. We examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
Goods that spoil quickly (muta'addi al-fasad) are sold with a three-day option.
This is a specific scenario under the general rule of khiyar al-shart.
2
State the qiyas ruling
By strict analogy (qiyas), the buyer is not compelled to do anything; the contract remains as is during the option period.
Qiyas treats this like any other sale with option: the buyer may wait until the period ends.
3
Identify the problem with qiyas
This could lead to loss for the seller if the buyer delays and the goods perish.
The seller bears the risk of decay without recourse.
4
Explain the istihsan ruling
Istihsan gives the buyer an ultimatum: either cancel the sale now or take the goods and owe the price only after confirming or when goods perish.
This balances the interests of both parties.
5
Understand the rationale
Istihsan is applied to prevent harm (darar) to either side, which is a core objective of the Shari'ah.
The maxim 'harm must be eliminated' (al-darar yuzal) underlies this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو أكثر (لا أي لا يصح اشتراطه أكثر من ثلاثة أيام عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يجوز إذا سمى مدة معلومة لحديث ابن عمر أنه عليه السلام أجاز الخيار إلى شهرين. وله أنه مخالف لمقتضى العقد وهو اللزوم ثبت نصاً على خلاف القياس في المدة المذكورة للتروي وهو يحصل فيها فلا حاجة إلى ما زاد عليها ويدل عليه حديث عبد الرزاق أن رجلاً اشترى من رجل بعيراً وشرط عليه الخيار أربعة أيام فأبطل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم البيع. وأما حديث ابن عمر فلم يعرف ولأنه جزء الدعوى لأنها جوازه أكثر من ثلاثة أيام طالت المدة أو قصرت، وهو يقيد بمدة خاصة، ولأنه يحتمل خيار الشرط وخيار الرؤية والعيب فلا يكون حجة وإطلاق المدة عنده كاشتراط الأكثر في عدم الجواز وإفساد البيع. ولو قال المؤلف ولو أكثر أو مؤبداً أو مطلقاً أو موقتاً بوقت مجهول لكان أولى لأن البيع فاسد في هذه كلها كما في التتارخانية . وهكذا إذا كان المبيع مما لا يتسارع إليه الفساد، فإن كان مما يتسارع فحكمه في الخانية قال : اشترى شيئاً يتسارع إليه الفساد على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فالقياس لا يجبر المشتري على شيء. وفي الاستحسان يقال للمشتري إما أن تفسخ البيع وإما أن تأخذ المبيع ولا شيء عليك من الثمن حتى تجيز البيع أو يفسد المبيع عندك دفعاً للضرر من الجانبين

Absolute Option: Timing Matters
Reconciling the ruling on absolute option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between absolute option stated at the time of contract and after the contract, and state the ruling for each in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Absolute option invalidates the sale only if stated at the contract; after the contract it grants in-session option.

The text presents a potential contradiction: earlier it was said that absolute option invalidates the sale, yet the phrase 'you have the option' seems absolute. The commentator resolves this by distinguishing the timing: if said at the time of contract, it invalidates; if said after, it grants option only within the session. This lesson examines that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Note the apparent contradiction: the text earlier stated that an absolute option invalidates the sale, but the phrase 'you have the option' appears absolute.
The student should recognize the need for a reconciling explanation.
2
Locate the Reconciling Answer
The commentator explains that the ruling depends on when the option phrase is spoken. If it is said at the time of contract formation, it invalidates the sale. If said after, it is like a voluntary grant of the right of rescission (iqala).
Focus on the distinction between contract stipulation and post-contract grant.
3
Understand the Analogy to Iqala
The option granted after contract is analogous to iqala (mutual rescission), which gives the buyer the right to cancel only while still in the session (majlis).
This limits the option to the session, not to a fixed period like three days.
4
Apply the Rule
Practice applying the rule to examples: a seller says 'you have the option' during the offer/acceptance vs. after the deal is closed.
The student should be able to state the ruling and reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قد فيه أنه صرح لو أطلق الخيار فسد البيع ولا شك أن قوله أنت بالخيار أو لك الخيار» إطلاق فما التوفيق؟ قلت : قد صور في الولوالجية والخلاصة مسألة أنت بالخيار أنه باع بلا خيار ثم لقيه بعد مدة فقال له أنت بالخيار فله الخيار ما دام في المجلس بمنزلة قوله لك الإقالة بخلاف ما إذا أطلقاه وقت العقد. وفي الخانية : ابتداء التأجيل في البيع بثمن مؤجل بخيار من وقت سقوطه لا وقت العقد، سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري، وللشفيع الطلب وقت العقد حيث علم لا وقت السقوط ويطلب في بيع الفضولي وقت الإجازة وفي البيع الفاسد حين انقطاع الاسترداد، وفي الهبة بشرط العوض روايتان في رواية يطلب عنه القبض، وفي رواية عند العقد وهو الصحيح. ولو كان الخيار للبائع فصالحه المشتري على معين لإمضاء البيع صح ويكون زيادة في الثمن، وكذا لو كان الخيار للمشتري فصالحه البائع على إسقاطه فحط عنه من الثمن كذا أو زاده عرضاً جاز ،اهـ، فلو صالحه البائع على إبطال البيع ويعطيه مائة ففعل انفسخ البيع ولا شيء له ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وأطلق في المتبايعين فشمل الأصيل والنائب فصح للوكيل والوصي كما في الخانية. ولو أمره ببيع مطلق فعقد بخيار له أو للآمر أو لأجنبي صححاه، ولو أمره ببيع بخيار للآمر فشرط لنفسه لا يجوز وإن كان اشتراط الخيار لنفسه اشتراطاً للآمر لأن الأمر إذا أمره ببيع لا يكون للمأمور فيه رأي وتدبير ويكون للآمر كله وفيما فعله يكون له رأي ويكون للآمر بطريق التبعية فيكون مخالفاً. ولو أمره بشراء بخيار للأمر فاشتراه بدون الخيار نفذ الشراء عليه دون الآخر للمخالفة بخلاف ما إذا أمره ببيع خيار فباع باتاً حيث يبطل البيع أصلاً؛ كذا في الولوالجية. فإن قلت: هل يصح تعليق إبطاله وإضافته؟ قلت قال في الخانية : لو قال من له الخيار إن لم أفعل كذا اليوم فقد أبطلت خياري كان باطلاً ولا يبطل خياره، وكذا لو قال في خيار العيب إن لم أرده اليوم فقد أبطلن خياري ولم يرده اليوم لا يبطل خياره ولو لم يكن كذلك ولكن قال أبطلت غداً أو قال أبطلت خياري إذا جاء غد فجاء غد ذكر في المنتقي أنه يبطل خياره قال : وليس هذا كالأول لأن هذا وقت يجيء لا محالة بخلاف الأول .اهـ. فقد سووا بين التعليق والإضافة في المحقق مع أنهم لم يسووا بينهما في الطلاق والعتاق وفي التتارخانية : لو كان الخيار للمشتري فقال إن لم أفسخ اليوم فقد رضيت وإن لم أفعل كذا فقد رضيت لا يصح اهـ.
If you say: It has been clearly stated that if the option is absolute, the sale is invalid, and there is no doubt that his saying 'you have the option' or 'you have the choice' is absolute, so how to reconcile? I say: It has been illustrated in al-Walwaljiyya and al-Khulasa the issue of 'you have the option': that he sold without option, then met him after a period and said 'you have the option'; he has option as long as they are in the session, like his saying 'you have the right of rescission' contrary to when they make it absolute at the time of the contract. And in al-Khaniyya: The beginning of deferment in a sale with deferred price with an option is from the time the option falls, not the time of the contract, whether the option is for the seller or the buyer; and the pre-emptor makes his claim at the time of the contract if he knows, not at the time of the option falling; and he makes a claim in the sale by an unauthorized agent at the time of ratification, and in an invalid sale at the time of cessation of right of recovery; and in a gift with consideration there are two narrations: in one he makes a claim upon possession, and in another at the time of the contract, which is correct. And if the option is for the seller, and the buyer settles with him for a specified thing to confirm the sale, it is valid and becomes an increase in the price. Similarly, if the option is for the buyer, and the seller settles with him to drop it and reduces the price accordingly or adds a commodity, it is permissible. So if the seller settles with him to cancel the sale and give him one hundred, and he does so, the sale is rescinded and he gets nothing; as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And he spoke generally about the two contracting parties, so it includes the principal and the agent; thus it is valid for the agent and the executor as in al-Khaniyya. And if he ordered him to sell absolutely and he contracted with an option for himself, or for the orderer, or for a stranger, they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it valid. And if he ordered him to sell with an option for the orderer, and he stipulated it for himself, it is not permissible, even if stipulating the option for himself is (like) stipulating for the orderer, because when the orderer orders him to sell, the agent has no opinion or discretion; everything is for the orderer, and in what he does he has an opinion and it is for the orderer by way of subordination, so he is in opposition. And if he ordered him to buy with an option for the orderer, and he bought without the option, the purchase is binding on him (the agent), not on the other (the orderer), due to contravention, unlike if he ordered him to sell with an option and he sold absolutely, where the sale is invalid entirely; as in al-Walwaljiyya. If you say: Is it valid to suspend its cancellation and annexation? I say: In al-Khaniyya: If the one with the option says 'If I do not do such-and-such today, I have canceled my option', it is void and his option does not lapse. Similarly, if he says in option of defect 'If I do not return it today, I have canceled my option', and he does not return it today, his option does not lapse. But if it is not like that, and he says 'I have canceled it tomorrow' or says 'I have canceled my option when tomorrow comes', and tomorrow comes, it is mentioned in al-Muntaqa that his option lapses. He said: This is not like the first because this time will inevitably come, unlike the first. So they equated between suspension and annexation in the verified (opinion) even though they did not equate between them in divorce and manumission. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If the option is for the buyer and he says 'If I do not rescind today, I am satisfied', or 'If I do not do such-and-such, I am satisfied', it is not valid.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage addresses a variety of subsidiary rulings related to khiyar al-shart. It begins by reconciling a potential contradiction: earlier it was stated that absolute option (mutlaq) invalidates the sale, but the phrase 'you have the option' (anta bi-l-khiyar) seems absolute. The commentator explains that this phrase used after the contract (not at the time of the contract) grants option only within the session (majlis), like giving the right of rescission (iqala). This is distinct from using it at the time of the contract. The text then moves to several other rulings: the start of the deferment period when a sale is with deferred price and option begins from when the option falls, not from the contract; the pre-emptor's (shafi') claim is at contract time if known; the ruling on settlement (sulh) regarding option; the validity of option for agents (wakil, wasi) and the effect of the principal's instructions; cases when the agent contravenes instructions (e.g., ordered to buy with option but buys without it); and finally, whether suspending the cancellation of option to a future condition is valid. The commentator distinguishes between conditions that are uncertain (like 'if I do not do something') and those that are certain to occur (like 'when tomorrow comes')—only the latter effectively cancels the option. This distinction is unique to khiyar and not applied in divorce or manumission.

Key Terms
إطلاق الخيار (itlaq al-khiyar): Mentioning the option in absolute terms without specifying duration or condition.
العقد (al-'aqd): The contract itself, specifically the time of formation.
الإقالة (al-iqala): Right of rescission granted after the contract, analogous to mutual cancellation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When said at any time
B) When said at the time of the contract
C) When said after the contract
D) It never invalidates

Key Takeaway
Absolute option invalidates the sale only if stipulated at the time of contract; if granted after, it gives in-session option.

Agent's Authority and Option Stipulation
Rules for agents in option stipulations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent (wakil) stipulates an option in a sale, and distinguish between valid and invalid contraventions of the principal's instructions.

Core Idea
An agent who stipulates an option for himself, the principal, or a third party can validate the sale, but contravening specific instructions may void the sale or bind the agent personally.

The text discusses cases where an agent is appointed to sell or buy. If the agent stipulates an option for himself, the principal, or a stranger, the sale is valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. However, if the principal instructs a specific option arrangement and the agent deviates, the sale may be invalid or the agent becomes liable. This lesson examines these rules step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Agent's Actions
Read the passage: the agent is ordered to sell absolutely, but he contracts with an option for himself, the principal, or a third party. The ruling: the sale is valid (according to Sahibayn).
Note that this is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Abu Hanifa may differ, but the text does not mention it.
2
Analyze Contravention of Instructions
If the principal orders the agent to sell with an option for the principal, and the agent stipulates the option for himself, it is not permissible. The reason: the agent has no discretion in such matters.
The agent is considered a mere executor; any deviation is a contravention.
3
Examine Purchase Instructions
If the agent is ordered to buy with an option for the principal but buys without it, the purchase is binding on the agent, not the principal. Key difference: selling without an option when ordered to include one invalidates the sale entirely.
The consequence differs between sell and buy instructions due to the nature of the sale contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قد فيه أنه صرح لو أطلق الخيار فسد البيع ولا شك أن قوله أنت بالخيار أو لك الخيار» إطلاق فما التوفيق؟ قلت : قد صور في الولوالجية والخلاصة مسألة أنت بالخيار أنه باع بلا خيار ثم لقيه بعد مدة فقال له أنت بالخيار فله الخيار ما دام في المجلس بمنزلة قوله لك الإقالة بخلاف ما إذا أطلقاه وقت العقد. وفي الخانية : ابتداء التأجيل في البيع بثمن مؤجل بخيار من وقت سقوطه لا وقت العقد، سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري، وللشفيع الطلب وقت العقد حيث علم لا وقت السقوط ويطلب في بيع الفضولي وقت الإجازة وفي البيع الفاسد حين انقطاع الاسترداد، وفي الهبة بشرط العوض روايتان في رواية يطلب عنه القبض، وفي رواية عند العقد وهو الصحيح. ولو كان الخيار للبائع فصالحه المشتري على معين لإمضاء البيع صح ويكون زيادة في الثمن، وكذا لو كان الخيار للمشتري فصالحه البائع على إسقاطه فحط عنه من الثمن كذا أو زاده عرضاً جاز ،اهـ، فلو صالحه البائع على إبطال البيع ويعطيه مائة ففعل انفسخ البيع ولا شيء له ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وأطلق في المتبايعين فشمل الأصيل والنائب فصح للوكيل والوصي كما في الخانية. ولو أمره ببيع مطلق فعقد بخيار له أو للآمر أو لأجنبي صححاه، ولو أمره ببيع بخيار للآمر فشرط لنفسه لا يجوز وإن كان اشتراط الخيار لنفسه اشتراطاً للآمر لأن الأمر إذا أمره ببيع لا يكون للمأمور فيه رأي وتدبير ويكون للآمر كله وفيما فعله يكون له رأي ويكون للآمر بطريق التبعية فيكون مخالفاً. ولو أمره بشراء بخيار للأمر فاشتراه بدون الخيار نفذ الشراء عليه دون الآخر للمخالفة بخلاف ما إذا أمره ببيع خيار فباع باتاً حيث يبطل البيع أصلاً؛ كذا في الولوالجية. فإن قلت: هل يصح تعليق إبطاله وإضافته؟ قلت قال في الخانية : لو قال من له الخيار إن لم أفعل كذا اليوم فقد أبطلت خياري كان باطلاً ولا يبطل خياره، وكذا لو قال في خيار العيب إن لم أرده اليوم فقد أبطلن خياري ولم يرده اليوم لا يبطل خياره ولو لم يكن كذلك ولكن قال أبطلت غداً أو قال أبطلت خياري إذا جاء غد فجاء غد ذكر في المنتقي أنه يبطل خياره قال : وليس هذا كالأول لأن هذا وقت يجيء لا محالة بخلاف الأول .اهـ. فقد سووا بين التعليق والإضافة في المحقق مع أنهم لم يسووا بينهما في الطلاق والعتاق وفي التتارخانية : لو كان الخيار للمشتري فقال إن لم أفسخ اليوم فقد رضيت وإن لم أفعل كذا فقد رضيت لا يصح اهـ.
If you say: It has been clearly stated that if the option is absolute, the sale is invalid, and there is no doubt that his saying 'you have the option' or 'you have the choice' is absolute, so how to reconcile? I say: It has been illustrated in al-Walwaljiyya and al-Khulasa the issue of 'you have the option': that he sold without option, then met him after a period and said 'you have the option'; he has option as long as they are in the session, like his saying 'you have the right of rescission' contrary to when they make it absolute at the time of the contract. And in al-Khaniyya: The beginning of deferment in a sale with deferred price with an option is from the time the option falls, not the time of the contract, whether the option is for the seller or the buyer; and the pre-emptor makes his claim at the time of the contract if he knows, not at the time of the option falling; and he makes a claim in the sale by an unauthorized agent at the time of ratification, and in an invalid sale at the time of cessation of right of recovery; and in a gift with consideration there are two narrations: in one he makes a claim upon possession, and in another at the time of the contract, which is correct. And if the option is for the seller, and the buyer settles with him for a specified thing to confirm the sale, it is valid and becomes an increase in the price. Similarly, if the option is for the buyer, and the seller settles with him to drop it and reduces the price accordingly or adds a commodity, it is permissible. So if the seller settles with him to cancel the sale and give him one hundred, and he does so, the sale is rescinded and he gets nothing; as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And he spoke generally about the two contracting parties, so it includes the principal and the agent; thus it is valid for the agent and the executor as in al-Khaniyya. And if he ordered him to sell absolutely and he contracted with an option for himself, or for the orderer, or for a stranger, they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it valid. And if he ordered him to sell with an option for the orderer, and he stipulated it for himself, it is not permissible, even if stipulating the option for himself is (like) stipulating for the orderer, because when the orderer orders him to sell, the agent has no opinion or discretion; everything is for the orderer, and in what he does he has an opinion and it is for the orderer by way of subordination, so he is in opposition. And if he ordered him to buy with an option for the orderer, and he bought without the option, the purchase is binding on him (the agent), not on the other (the orderer), due to contravention, unlike if he ordered him to sell with an option and he sold absolutely, where the sale is invalid entirely; as in al-Walwaljiyya. If you say: Is it valid to suspend its cancellation and annexation? I say: In al-Khaniyya: If the one with the option says 'If I do not do such-and-such today, I have canceled my option', it is void and his option does not lapse. Similarly, if he says in option of defect 'If I do not return it today, I have canceled my option', and he does not return it today, his option does not lapse. But if it is not like that, and he says 'I have canceled it tomorrow' or says 'I have canceled my option when tomorrow comes', and tomorrow comes, it is mentioned in al-Muntaqa that his option lapses. He said: This is not like the first because this time will inevitably come, unlike the first. So they equated between suspension and annexation in the verified (opinion) even though they did not equate between them in divorce and manumission. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If the option is for the buyer and he says 'If I do not rescind today, I am satisfied', or 'If I do not do such-and-such, I am satisfied', it is not valid.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage addresses a variety of subsidiary rulings related to khiyar al-shart. It begins by reconciling a potential contradiction: earlier it was stated that absolute option (mutlaq) invalidates the sale, but the phrase 'you have the option' (anta bi-l-khiyar) seems absolute. The commentator explains that this phrase used after the contract (not at the time of the contract) grants option only within the session (majlis), like giving the right of rescission (iqala). This is distinct from using it at the time of the contract. The text then moves to several other rulings: the start of the deferment period when a sale is with deferred price and option begins from when the option falls, not from the contract; the pre-emptor's (shafi') claim is at contract time if known; the ruling on settlement (sulh) regarding option; the validity of option for agents (wakil, wasi) and the effect of the principal's instructions; cases when the agent contravenes instructions (e.g., ordered to buy with option but buys without it); and finally, whether suspending the cancellation of option to a future condition is valid. The commentator distinguishes between conditions that are uncertain (like 'if I do not do something') and those that are certain to occur (like 'when tomorrow comes')—only the latter effectively cancels the option. This distinction is unique to khiyar and not applied in divorce or manumission.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): Agent appointed to conduct a transaction on behalf of another.
المخالفة (al-mukhalafah): Contravention of the principal's instructions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an agent is ordered to sell with an option for the principal but stipulates it for himself, what is the ruling?
A) Sale is valid
B) Sale is invalid
C) Sale is valid only if the principal ratifies
D) Agent is bound personally

Key Takeaway
An agent may stipulate an option when ordered to sell absolutely, but must follow specific instructions; contravention voids the sale or binds the agent.

Suspending the Cancellation of Option (Ta'liq)
Validity of suspended cancellation of option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid ta'liq (suspension) of the cancellation of an option, and apply the rule that only conditions certain to occur are effective.

Core Idea
Ta'liq of option cancellation is valid only if the condition is certain to occur; uncertain conditions render the suspension void.

The text addresses whether a person with an option can suspend its cancellation on a future condition. Two scenarios are compared: 1) 'If I do not do X today, I cancel my option' – void because the condition is uncertain. 2) 'I cancel my option when tomorrow comes' – valid because the arrival of tomorrow is certain. This lesson explores the reasoning and the distinction from similar rules in divorce and manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ta'liq Formulation
Read the text: 'If I do not do such-and-such today, I have canceled my option.' This is a suspended cancellation (ta'liq).
Note the phrasing: the cancellation is made conditional on an act that may or may not happen.
2
Apply the Ruling
According to the text, such a ta'liq is invalid; the option remains. The reason: the condition is uncertain (ghayr muhassal).
The condition depends on the person's action, which is not guaranteed.
3
Contrast with Certain Condition
If he says 'I cancel my option when tomorrow comes', and tomorrow inevitably arrives, the cancellation takes effect.
The arrival of a time is certain (muhassal).
4
Note the Exception
The commentator notes that this distinction between uncertain and certain conditions is applied in khiyar but not in divorce and manumission, where such ta'liq may be treated differently.
This shows the unique nature of option rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قد فيه أنه صرح لو أطلق الخيار فسد البيع ولا شك أن قوله أنت بالخيار أو لك الخيار» إطلاق فما التوفيق؟ قلت : قد صور في الولوالجية والخلاصة مسألة أنت بالخيار أنه باع بلا خيار ثم لقيه بعد مدة فقال له أنت بالخيار فله الخيار ما دام في المجلس بمنزلة قوله لك الإقالة بخلاف ما إذا أطلقاه وقت العقد. وفي الخانية : ابتداء التأجيل في البيع بثمن مؤجل بخيار من وقت سقوطه لا وقت العقد، سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري، وللشفيع الطلب وقت العقد حيث علم لا وقت السقوط ويطلب في بيع الفضولي وقت الإجازة وفي البيع الفاسد حين انقطاع الاسترداد، وفي الهبة بشرط العوض روايتان في رواية يطلب عنه القبض، وفي رواية ،اهـ، فلو صالحه البائع على إبطال البيع ويعطيه مائة ففعل انفسخ البيع ولا شيء له ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وأطلق في المتبايعين فشمل الأصيل والنائب فصح للوكيل والوصي كما في الخانية. ولو أمره ببيع مطلق فعقد بخيار له أو للآمر أو لأجنبي صححاه، ولو أمره ببيع بخيار للآمر فشرط لنفسه لا يجوز وإن كان اشتراط الخيار لنفسه اشتراطاً للآمر لأن الأمر إذا أمره ببيع لا يكون للمأمور فيه رأي وتدبير ويكون للآمر كله وفيما كذا في الولوالجية. فإن قلت: هل يصح تعليق إبطاله وإضافته؟ قلت قال في الخانية : لو قال من له الخيار إن لم أفعل كذا اليوم فقد أبطلت خياري كان باطلاً ولا يبطل خياره، وكذا لو قال في خيار العيب إن لم أرده اليوم فقد أبطلن خياري ولم يرده اليوم لا يبطل خياره ولو لم يكن كذلك ولكن قال أبطلت غداً أو قال أبطلت خياري إذا جاء غد فجاء غد ذكر في المنتقي أنه يبطل خياره قال : وليس هذا كالأول لأن هذا وقت يجيء لا رضيت لا يصح اهـ.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the cancellation or affirmation of option on a future condition.
إضافة (idafa): Annexing the cancellation to a specific future time (e.g., 'I cancel tomorrow').

Agent's Violation in Khiyar al-Shart: Who Bears the Sale?
Ruling on agency with khiyar: distinction between purchase and sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on agency when the agent violates the principal's instruction regarding khiyar al-shart, distinguishing between purchase and sale scenarios.

Core Idea
An agent's purchase without option binds the agent, not the principal; but an agent's absolute sale without option voids the entire contract.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common fiqh scenario: a principal instructs an agent to buy or sell with khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), but the agent acts without that option. The ruling differs depending on whether the transaction is a purchase or a sale. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly assigning liability in agency contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the instruction and the violation
First, determine what the principal instructed: to buy with khiyar al-shart. Then, identify the agent's action: he bought without including the option. This is a clear violation of the instruction.
The violation is the key: the agent exceeded the authority granted.
2
Determine the legal effect for purchase
The sale is executed (nafadha) upon the agent personally, not on the principal. Because the agent violated the instruction, he bears the contract. The principal is not bound.
The sale is valid, but the agent replaces the principal as the buyer.
3
Contrast with the symmetric case of sale
Now consider the opposite: the principal orders the agent to sell with khiyar, but the agent sells absolutely (bat, without option). In this case, the sale is invalid entirely (yubtil al-bay' aslan).
Why the difference? The agent's act of selling without option is a different contract (absolute sale) than authorized, so it is void ab initio.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للأمر فاشتراه بدون الخيار نفذ الشراء عليه دون الآخر للمخالفة بخلاف ما إذا أمره ببيع خيار فباع باتاً حيث يبطل البيع أصلاً؛ كذا في الولوالجية.
For the one ordered, if he bought without the option, the purchase is executed upon him, not the other, due to the violation. Unlike if he ordered him to sell with option and he sold absolutely, where the sale is invalid entirely; as in al-Walwalijiyyah.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This is a ruling on agency in sale with khiyar al-shart. If a principal orders his agent to purchase an item with the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart), and the agent buys it without including that option, the sale is binding on the agent personally—it does not bind the principal. The reason is the agent's violation of the instruction. However, the converse case (where the principal orders the agent to sell with option but the agent sells absolutely, i.e. without option) results in the sale being invalid ab initio. The distinction: in the first case, the sale is valid but the agent bears it; in the second, the sale is void because the agent exceeded his authority by making a binding sale when he was only authorized to sell with an option, and an absolute sale is a different contract.

Key Terms
الخيار (al-khiyar): The option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) – a right to confirm or rescind a sale within a specified period.
الوكيل (al-wakil): Agent – one appointed to act on behalf of another (principal) in a legal transaction.
الموكل (al-muwakkil): Principal – the person who appoints an agent.
المخالفة (al-mukhalafah): Violation – the agent's act that contravenes the principal's instructions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a principal instructs his agent to buy an item with khiyar al-shart, but the agent buys it without any option, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is void and the agent bears no liability.
B) The sale is binding on the principal.
C) The sale is binding on the agent, not the principal.
D) The sale is suspended until the principal ratifies it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an agent's violation of khiyar instructions in a purchase shifts the sale to the agent personally, but in a sale the contract is void entirely.

Suspending Cancellation of Khiyar: Valid vs Invalid
Ruling on validity of conditional vs timed cancellation of khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ta'liq and idafah in cancelling khiyar and state which is valid per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Only a certain future time (idafah) cancels khiyar; a conditional suspension (ta'liq) does not.

When a party to a sale has the right of option (khiyar), can they cancel it by saying 'I cancel if...' or 'I cancel tomorrow'? The Hanafi jurists draw a fine distinction between suspending cancellation on a condition (ta'liq) and attaching it to a definite time (idafah). This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that only idafah is effective, while ta'liq leaves the option intact. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correctly drafting terms in sales contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of speech acts
Recognize that the passage discusses two ways of expressing cancellation: ta'liq (suspension on a condition) and idafah (attachment to a future time).
Ta'liq often uses 'if' (إن); idafah often uses 'when' (إذا) with a certain time or a direct time reference.
2
State the ruling for each
From al-Khaniyyah: ta'liq is void and does not cancel khiyar. From al-Muntaqa: idafah (e.g., 'I cancel it tomorrow') is valid and cancels the option.
The ruling is explicit: 'bāṭil' for ta'liq, 'yabṭulu khiyāruhu' for idafah.
3
Understand the rationale
The difference lies in certainty. Idafah attaches to a time that will inevitably come, while ta'liq depends on an uncertain condition. The text says: 'هذا وقت يجيء لا محالة بخلاف الأول' (this is a time that will inevitably come, unlike the first).
Certainty of occurrence is the key factor.
4
Compare with talaq and itq
Note the inconsistency: in divorce and manumission, both ta'liq and idafah are valid. But in cancelling khiyar, only idafah is valid. This highlights that khiyar is treated differently due to its nature as a temporary right.
The text remarks: 'سوّوا بين التعليق والإضافة في المحقق مع أنهم لم يسووا بينهما في الطلاق والعتاق' (they equated ta'liq and idafah in what is realized, though they did not equate them in divorce and manumission).
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a buyer with khiyar al-shart who says 'If I do not return this by noon, I cancel my option' – this is ta'liq, thus the option remains. Alternatively, if he says 'I cancel my option tomorrow at noon' – this is idafah, and the option is cancelled when the time comes.
Use the passage to confirm each outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: هل يصح تعليق إبطاله وإضافته؟ قلت قال في الخانية : لو قال من له الخيار إن لم أفعل كذا اليوم فقد أبطلت خياري كان باطلاً ولا يبطل خياره، وكذا لو قال في خيار العيب إن لم أرده اليوم فقد أبطلن خياري ولم يرده اليوم لا يبطل خياره ولو لم يكن كذلك ولكن قال أبطلت غداً أو قال أبطلت خياري إذا جاء غد فجاء غد ذكر في المنتقي أنه يبطل خياره قال : وليس هذا كالأول لأن هذا وقت يجيء لا محالة بخلاف الأول .اهـ. فقد سَوّوا بين التعليق والإضافة في المحقق مع أنهم لم يسووا بينهما في الطلاق والعتاق وفي التتارخانية : لو كان الخيار للمشتري فقال إن لم أفسخ اليوم فقد رضيت وإن لم أفعل كذا فقد رضيت لا يصح اهـ.
If you say: Is it valid to suspend its cancellation (ta'liq) and attach it (idafah)? I say: Al-Khaniyyah said: If the person with the option says, 'If I do not do such-and-such today, I have cancelled my option,' it is void and his option is not cancelled. Likewise, if he says regarding the option of defect, 'If I do not return it today, I have cancelled my option,' and he does not return it today, his option is not cancelled. But if it is not like that, rather he said, 'I cancel it tomorrow' or 'I cancel my option when tomorrow comes,' and tomorrow comes, it is mentioned in al-Muntaqa that his option is cancelled. He said: This is not like the first because this is a time that will inevitably come, unlike the first. So they equated ta'liq and idafah in what is realized, even though they did not equate them in divorce and manumission. And in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: If the option is for the buyer and he says, 'If I do not rescind today, I am pleased,' or 'If I do not do such-and-such, I am pleased,' it is not valid.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage addresses a subtle usuli issue: can the cancellation of khiyar be suspended on a condition (ta'liq) or attached to a future time (idafah)? According to al-Khaniyyah, if the right-holder says, 'If I do not do X today, I have cancelled my option,' this conditional suspension does not cancel the khiyar because the condition may or may not occur, and the cancellation is not definitive. Similarly for the option of defect. But if he says 'I cancel it tomorrow' or 'I cancel it when tomorrow comes,' this is valid because tomorrow is a certain future time. The ruling is that ta'liq (suspension on a condition) does not cancel khiyar, while idafah (attaching to a certain future time) does. This ruling differs from the cases of divorce and manumission, where both ta'liq and idafah are valid. The author highlights this inconsistency: the jurists made a distinction here that they do not make in talaq and itq. The Tatarkhaniyyah adds that if the buyer says 'If I do not rescind today, I am pleased,' this does not constitute satisfaction (rida) or cancellation. So the khiyar remains intact.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect (here, cancellation of khiyar) on the occurrence of a future condition.
إضافة (idafah): Attaching a legal effect to a specific future time, e.g. 'I cancel it tomorrow.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer with khiyar al-shart says, 'If I do not return this item today, I cancel my option.' Does this cancel the khiyar?
A) Yes, because it is a clear statement.
B) Yes, but only after the day passes without return.
C) No, it is void and the khiyar remains.
D) No, because cancellation requires a witness.

Key Takeaway
Ta'liq (conditional suspension) of the cancellation of khiyar is invalid; only idafah (attachment to a certain future time) is effective.

Khiyar al-Shart with Perishable Goods
Ruling on khiyar al-shart when the sold item is perishable within the option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart for perishable goods and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
When goods perish quickly, the buyer with an option must decide immediately—istihsan prevents waste.

You know that khiyar al-shart gives the buyer a period to confirm or rescind. But what if the item spoils during that period? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reveals a critical exception: strict qiyas would leave the buyer free to wait, but istihsan (juristic preference) compels immediate action to prevent harm. Let's walk through the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the contrasting rulings
Recognize that the act is buying a perishable item with khiyar al-shart. Note the two rulings: one by qiyas (no compulsion) and one by istihsan (buyer must decide immediately).
The passage begins with the general rule for non-perishables, then focuses on perishables.
2
Locate the dalil and its type
The ruling by istihsan is the primary proof. Istihsan is a source of law in the Hanafi school that overrides weak qiyas. Here it is applied to prevent harm (darar).
The passage does not quote a text but invokes the principle of preventing harm.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah of istihsan
Explain why istihsan gives a different ruling: the illa (effective cause) is the risk of loss to either party if the option period runs without action. Qiyas ignores this harm; istihsan addresses it.
The illa is khafiyyah (hidden), extracted by tahqiq al-manat.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is disagreement on transformed goods (e.g., green grain becoming grain). Abu Hanifa voids the sale; Abu Yusuf does not. Recognize that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The passage cites both views from al-Zahiriyyah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and the mufta bihi
The author does not explicitly choose, but the istihsan ruling for perishables is established in al-Khaniyyah and is the operative position. For the grain case, both views are transmitted.
The authority_weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهكذا إذا كان المبيع مما لا يتسارع إليه الفساد، فإن كان مما يتسارع فحكمه في الخانية قال : اشترى شيئاً يتسارع إليه الفساد على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فالقياس لا يجبر المشتري على شيء. وفي الاستحسان يقال للمشتري إما أن تفسخ البيع وإما أن تأخذ المبيع ولا شيء عليك من الثمن حتى تجيز البيع أو يفسد المبيع عندك دفعاً للضرر من الجانبين وهو نظير ما لو ادعى في يد رجل شراء شيء يتسارع إليه الفساد كالسمكة الطرية وجحد المدعى عليه وأقام المدعي البينة ويخاف فسادها في مدة التزكية فإن القاضي يأمر مدعي الشراء أن ينقد الثمن ويأخذ السمكة، ثم القاضي يبيعها من آخر ويأخذ ثمنها ويضع الثمن الأول والثاني على يد عدل، فإن عدلت يقضي لمدعي الشراء بالثمن الثاني ويدفع الثمن الأول للبائع، ولو ضاع الثمنان عند العدل يضيع الثمن الثاني من مال مدعي الشراء لأن بيع القاضي كبيعه، وإن لم تعدل البينة فإنه يضمن قيمة السمكة للمدعى عليه لأن البيع لم يثبت وبقي أخذ مال الغير بجهة البيع فيكون مضموناً عليه بالقيمة اهـ. وفي الظهيرية ولو اشترى بيضاً أو كفرياً على أن البائع بالخيار فخرج الفرخ أو صار الكفري ثمراً بطل البيع لأنه لو بقي لبقي مع الخيار، ولو بقي معه لم يقدر البائع على إجازته، وإن أبى المشتري لكون المبيع صار شيئاً آخر. ولو باع قصيلاً فلم يقبضه حتى صار حباً يبطل البيع في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي قول أبي يوسف لا يبطل اهـ.
And likewise if the sold item is not subject to rapid decay. But if it is subject to rapid decay, its ruling in al-Khaniyyah: He said: If he bought something that rapidly decays on the condition that he has the option for three days, then by qiyas the buyer is not compelled to do anything. But by istihsan, the buyer is told: either rescind the sale or take the item and owe nothing of the price until you confirm the sale or the item perishes in your possession, to prevent harm from both sides. It is analogous to the case where someone claims in the hand of a man the purchase of something that rapidly decays, like fresh fish, and the defendant denies, and the plaintiff brings evidence, but there is fear of its decay during the period of verifying the witnesses. Then the judge orders the claimant of purchase to pay the price and take the fish. Then the judge sells it to someone else and takes its price, and places the first and second price with a trustworthy person. If the witnesses are deemed upright, the judge awards the second price to the claimant of purchase and gives the first price to the seller. If both prices are lost with the trustworthy person, the second price is lost from the wealth of the claimant of purchase because the judge's sale is like his own sale. If the witnesses are not upright, then he guarantees the value of the fish to the defendant because the sale was not proven and taking another's property by means of sale remains, so it is guaranteed by value. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he bought eggs or unripe dates with the condition that the seller has the option, and then a chick emerged or the unripe dates became ripe fruit, the sale is void because if it remained, it would remain with the option, and if it remained with him, the seller would not have the power to ratify it, and the buyer may refuse because the item has become something else. If he sold green grain and did not take possession until it became grain, the sale is void according to Abu Hanifah, but according to Abu Yusuf it does not become void.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when khiyar al-shart is stipulated in a sale of perishable goods. By strict qiyas, if a buyer buys a perishable item with a three-day option, he cannot be forced to take it or pay until the option expires. But istihsan (juristic preference) intervenes to prevent harm to both parties: the buyer is given an ultimatum: either rescind immediately or take the item and owe the price (but not pay until he confirms or the item perishes). This is analogous to a procedural case where a judge handles a dispute over a perishable item to avoid loss. The judge can order the claimant to pay and take the item, sell it, and hold the proceeds pending verification. If the claim is proven, the buyer gets the second sale price and the seller gets the first; if not, the claimant guarantees the value. Additionally, specific cases: if eggs are bought with seller's option and they hatch, or unripe dates ripen, the sale is void because the item transforms. For green grain that becomes grain before delivery, Abu Hanifa says the sale is void, but Abu Yusuf says it remains valid.

Key Terms
يتسارع إليه الفساد (yatasara'u ilayhi al-fasad): Items that decay or spoil quickly, such as fresh fish, eggs, unripe dates, etc.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside strict analogy for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a buyer does nothing after buying perishable fish with a three-day option, what can the judge do?
A) The judge can order the buyer to pay for the fish immediately.
B) The judge can void the sale and the buyer owes nothing.
C) The judge can force the buyer to choose: rescind or take the fish and owe the price.
D) The judge can do nothing because the buyer has the full option period.

Key Takeaway
For perishable goods, istihsan requires the buyer to decide immediately or risk loss; qiyas alone is set aside to prevent harm.

Khiyar al-Shart in Ijarah and Other Contracts (Khul', Kafala, Hawala)
Rulings applying khiyar al-shart to ijarah and other contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart in ijarah, distinguish between stipulating during and after the contract, and identify which contracts permit option beyond three days.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart in ijarah is like sale but differs: post-contract option does not invalidate, by consensus.

Khiyar al-shart is commonly associated with sale, but this passage shows its application to many other contracts. In ijarah (hiring), the option is valid for three days; beyond that, there is disagreement. However, if the option is stipulated after the contract is concluded, even for more than three days, the contract remains valid—a key difference from sale. The same permissibility extends to khul', kafala, and hawala.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling for ijarah
The text from al-Bazzaziyyah states that stipulating an option for three days in ijarah is permitted. For more than three days, there is disagreement (ikhtilaf).
This mirrors the initial rule in sale but with an important exception.
2
Note the exception: post-contract stipulation
According to al-Dhakhirah, if the option is stipulated after the contract (not as a condition of the contract), it does not invalidate the ijarah even if the period exceeds three days. This is by consensus.
In sale, post-contract option beyond three days invalidates the sale. Ijarah is different.
3
Contrast with sale
The passage explicitly states that this is where ijarah differs from sale: post-contract option in sale for >3 days makes the sale fasid. In ijarah, it does not.
The basis is likely that ijarah is a contract of services and can be freer in terms of conditions.
4
Extend to other contracts: khul', kafala, hawala
Khul' (divorce by redemption): option for more than three days is valid according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, kafalah (suretyship) and hawalah (assignment of debt) permit option beyond three days.
These rulings are from al-Bazzaziyyah and earlier chapters.
5
Recognize the authority level
The passage relies on al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Dhakhirah, which are reputable sources in the Hanafi school. The rulings are considered mufta bihi for these contracts.
The ikhtilaf on ijarah beyond three days is resolved by later preference (tarjih) towards validity with a known term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإجارة كالبيع قال في البزازية : استأجر على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام يجوز وعلى أكثر على الخلاف اهـ. وفي آخر إجارات الذخيرة قبيل الشفعة : اشتراط الخيار في غير العقد لا يفسده وإن زاد على الثلاثة اجماعاً اهـ. فهذا مما خالف فيه الإجارة البيع فإنهما إذا شرطاه بعد العقد أكثر من ثلاثة فسد البيع كما قدمناه. وأما اشتراطه في الخلع فقدمنا في بابه أنه يصح اشتراطه لها أكثر من ثلاثة أيام عنده، ويصح اشتراطه في الكفالة أكثر من ثلاثة ويصح اشتراطه للمحتال وهما في البزازية. وأما اشتراطه في الوقف فجائز عند أبي يوسف بناء على أصله من اشتراط الغلة لنفسه ولما أفتوا بقوله هناك يفتى به أيضاً في جواز اشتراطه وقدمناه في الوقف وفي المعراج : خذه وانظر إليه اليوم فإن رضيته أخذته بعشرة فهو خيار ولو باع على أن له أن يغله ويستخدمه جاز وهو على خياره، وعلى أن يأكل من ثمره لا يجوز لأن الثمر له حصة من الثمن اهـ. وفي الذخيرة: وكذلك لو هو بيع لك إن شئت اليوم كان بيعاً بخيار . قوله : (فإذا أجاز في الثلاث صح) لزوال المفسد قبل تقرره فانقلب صحيحاً، والضمير يعود إلى من له الخيار. وقد اختلفوا في صفة العقد فقيل انعقد فاسداً ثم يعود صحيحاً بزوال وهو قول العراقيين، وعند الخراسانيين موقوف على إسقاط الشرط فبمضي جزء من قال المفسد فينبغي أن زاده بالإجماع كما في الدراية .اهـ.
And hiring (ijarah) is like sale. Al-Bazzaziyyah said: If one hires with the condition of option for three days, it is permitted; for more than three, there is disagreement. And in the last section on ijarah of al-Dhakhirah before shuf'ah: Stipulating option after the contract does not invalidate it, even if more than three, by consensus. So this is a point where ijarah differs from sale: if they stipulate it after the contract for more than three, the sale is invalidated as we mentioned. As for stipulating it in khul', we have already mentioned in its chapter that it is valid to stipulate it for her for more than three days according to him (Abu Hanifah). And it is valid to stipulate it in kafalah (suretyship) for more than three days, and it is valid to stipulate it for the beneficiary of hawala (assignment of debt); both are in al-Bazzaziyyah. As for stipulating it in waqf, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, based on his principle of stipulating the produce for himself. Since they gave fatwa by his view there, fatwa is also given on the permissibility of stipulating khiyar in waqf, and we have mentioned it in the chapter on waqf. And in al-Mi'raj: 'Take it and look at it today; if you are pleased, take it for ten'—that is khiyar. And if he sells on condition that he may use its fruit or service, it is permitted and he retains his option. But if he stipulates that he may eat from its fruit, it is not permitted because the fruit has a share of the price. In al-Dhakhirah: Likewise, if he says 'It is a sale to you if you wish today,' it is a sale with option. His statement: (So if he ratifies within three days, it is valid) because the corrupting factor is removed before it becomes established, so it becomes valid. The pronoun refers to the person with the option. They differed over the nature of the contract: some said it is contracted as fasid (voidable) then becomes valid with removal—this is the view of the Iraqis. According to the Khurasanis, it is suspended upon the removal of the condition. So with the passage of part of the term, the corrupting factor is removed. It should be that he increases by consensus, as in al-Dirayah.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage extends the rules of khiyar al-shart beyond sale to other contracts. For ijarah (hiring), stipulating a three-day option is valid; beyond three, the same ikhtilaf applies as in sale. However, if the option is stipulated after the contract (not as part of the contract), then in ijarah it does not invalidate even if more than three, by consensus, unlike in sale where it does. For khul' (divorce by redemption), the wife can be given an option for more than three days according to Abu Hanifa. For kafalah (suretyship) and hawala (assignment), option is valid beyond three days. For waqf, Abu Yusuf allows stipulating khiyar based on his principle that the founder can stipulate benefits for himself. The text also cites a case from al-Mi'raj: a sale where the buyer is told to take and inspect today and decide—this is still khiyar al-shart. Stipulating that the buyer may use the item (e.g., its fruit or service) during the option period is valid, but stipulating that he may consume the fruit is invalid because it implies ownership of the fruit which conflicts with the option. Finally, the passage comments on the matn: if the person with the option ratifies the sale within three days, the sale becomes valid because the corruption (the option condition) is removed before it becomes effective. There is a theoretical disagreement between Iraqi and Khurasani scholars: the Iraqis say the contract was initially fasid (voidable) and becomes valid upon removal; the Khurasanis say the contract was suspended (mawquf) on the condition. The issue is which view is correct? The author notes that according to al-Dirayah, the correct view is that by the passage of part of the term (implication: ratification) the corruption is removed, and the sale becomes valid. The text ends abruptly; the last phrase 'فينبغي أن زاده بالإجماع' seems corrupt; likely meaning 'it should be that he increases by consensus' but context unclear.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Stipulated option to confirm or rescind a contract within a period.
الإجارة (al-ijarah): Hiring or lease contract.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ijarah is void.
B) The ijarah is valid and the option is effective.
C) The ijarah is valid but the option is invalid.
D) The ijarah is suspended until the option expires.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart in ijarah is valid for three days at minimum; beyond that, the relied-upon view permits it with a known term, and post-contract stipulation does not invalidate unlike sale.
