الثالث بعشرة وهذا بعشرين وهذا بثلاثين فاحمل الثياب إلى منزلك فأي ثوب ترضى بعته منك، فحمل فهلكت عند المشتري قال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل : إن هلكت الكل جملة أو على التعاقب ولا يدري الذي هلك أولاً ولا الذي بعده ضمن المشتري ثلث كل ثوب، وإن عرف الأول لزمه ذلك الثوب والثوبان أمانة عنده، وإن هلكت الثوبان وبقي الثالث فإنه يرد الثالث لأنه أمانة وأما الثوبان يلزمه نصف ثمن كل واحد منهما إذا كان لا يعلم أيها هلك أولاً، وإن هلك واحد وبقي ثوبان يلزمه ثمن الهالك ويرد الثوبين، وإن احترق الثوبان ونقص الثالث ثلثه أو ربعه ولا يعلم أيهما احترق أولاً يرد ما بقي من ولا يضمن نقصان الحرق بقدره ويلزمه نصف ثمن كل واحد من الثوبين اهـ. فهذا صريح في أن بيان الثمن من جهة البائع يكفي للضمان. وفي الخلاصة والبزازية : اذهب به إن رضيته اشتریت فذهب به فضاع لا يضمن ولو قال إن رضيته اشتريته بعشرة فذهب به وضاع ضمن اهـ. وهذا صريح فيما قلناه وقد اشتبه عليه المقبوض على سوم الشراء بالمقبوض على وجه النظر فإن فيما نقله عن القنية إنما قال المساوم حتى أنظر إليه والمقبوض على وجه النظر أمانة، وما ذكرناه عن أصحاب الفتاوى إنما قال إن رضيته اشتريته والدليل على الفرق بينهما أن يكون سبباً كالعتق إذ سببه إنما هو القرابة فتدبره قوله : (وهذا صريح فيما قلناه) قال الرملي : الظاهر أن ذلك صادر من المشتري لا من البائع فكان شاهداً عليه لا له، نعم ما تقدم عن الخانية صريح فيما قاله فتأمل اهـ . قلت : ونقل الطرسوسي عن الخانية أيضاً: رجل يبيع سلعة فقال لغيره أنظر فيها فأخذها لينظر فيها فهلكت في يده لا يضمن وإن قال الناظر بعد ما نظر بكم تبيع قالوا يكون ضامناً، والصحيح أنه لا يكون ضامناً إلا إذا قال صاحب السلعة بكذا اهـ. وأوله الطرسوسي بما إذا قال المشتري أيضاً بكذا ليوافق ما حمل عليه كلامهم من عدم الاكتفاء ببيان الثمن من البائع فقط، وهذا يبعد ما في شرح نظم الكنز للعلامة المقدسي من أن المؤلف لم يدر مراد الطرسوسي فحمله على الخطأ وذلك أنه أراد أنه لا بد من تسمية الثمن من الجانبين حقيقة أو حكماً. أما الأول فظاهر، وأما الثاني فبأن . أحدهما ويصدر من الآخر ما يدل على الرضا به كما في قوله هاته فإن أخذته بعشرة فإن تسليمه بعد قوله دليل الرضا بخلاف قوله حتى انظر فإنه لم يوافقه على ما سمى بل جعله مغياً بالنظر وأعرض عما سمى وجميع ما ذكروه وفيه تسمية أحدهما وحكموا بالضمان القسم الثاني عند التأمل، ومن نظر عبارة الطرسوسي وجدها تنادي بما ذكرناه اهـ. ولم أر في كلام الطرسوسي ما ينادي بما ذكره بل الذي صرح به أن الضمان فيما لو ذكر البائع والمساوم في حالة المساومة ثمناً أو ذكره المشتري وحده وقال أيضاً: ولو كان يكتفي بذكر الثمن من جهة البائع وحده لكان يجب الضمان في قولهم قال صاحب الثوب هو بعشرة أو أخذه بعشرة وقال المساوم هاته حتى أنظر إليه وقبضه وضاع وهلك في يده أنه يضمن وقد نصوا في جميع الكتب أنه على سوم الضمان ما في الخانية قال : ولو أخذ ثوباً على المساومة فدفعه إليه البائع وهو يساومه والبائع يقول هو بعشرة فهو على الثمن الذي قال البائع حتى يرد عليه المشتري، وإن ساومه فقال المشتري حتى أنظر إليه فدفعه فضاع منه فليس على المشتري شيء لأنه إنما أخذه للنظر، وإن أخذه على غير النظر ثم قال حتى انظر إله فقوله حتى أنظر إليه لا يخرجه عن اهـ. فهذا صريح في الفرق بينهما وفي الذخيرة معزياً لأبي يوسف: رجل ساوم رجلاً بثوب فقال صاحب الثوب هو بعشرة فقال المساوم هاته حتى أنظر إليه فدفعه إليه على ذلك فضاع لا يلزمه شيء. علل فقال : لأنه أخذه على النظر إشارة إلى أن هذا ليس بمقبوض الشراء اهـ. فهذا صريح في الفرق بينهما أيضاً. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية: رجل قال هذا الثوب لك بعشرة فقال هاته حتى أنظر إليه أو قال حتى أريه غيري فأخذه على ذلك فضاع في يده لم يضمن في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ولو قال هاته فإن رضيته أخذته فضاع كان عليه الثمن اهـ. وهذا صريح أيضاً فثبت بهذه النقول من الكتب المعتمدة أنه لا فرق في المقبوض على سوم الشراء بين بيان الثمن من البائع أو من المشتري وحده، ولقد صدق ختام المحققين ابن الهمام في فتح القدير حيث قال في كتاب الوقف : إن الطرسوسي بعيد عن الفقه، ثم رأيت الفرق بينهما أيضاً صريحاً في فروق الكرابيسي ومنها نقلت قال : لو قال هذا الثوب لك بعشرة فقال هاته حتى أنظر إليه أو حتى أريه غيري فأخذه فضاع قال أبو حنيفة : لا شيء عليه يعني يهلك أمانة وإن قال هاته حتى أنظر إليه فإن رضيته أخذته فهلك فعليه الثمن. والفرق أن في الفصل الأول أمره لينظر إليه أو ليريه غيره وذلك ليس ببيع، فأما في الفصل الآخر أمره بالإتيان به ليرضاه ويأخذه وذلك بيع بدون الأمر فمع الأمر أولى اهـ.
والظاهر من كلامهم أنه لا فرق بين الهلاك أو الاستهلاك، وما في الذخيرة عن أبي يوسف أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء مضمون بالثمن محمول على القيمة، وما ذكره لا يضمن ونصوا في جميع الصور التي فيها ذكر الثمن من جهة المساوم وحده أنه يضمن اهـ. وبعد هذا فالظاهر أن المراد هو ما قاله المقدسي وإن كان بعيداً من كلام الطرسوسي وذلك أن التسمية إذا كانت من المشتري تصح باعتبار أن البائع لما سلمه المبيع صار راضياً بها فكذا إذا كانت من البائع و قبضه المشتري راضياً بها .
قوله : (فأما في الفصل الآخر الخ) قال في النهر وأقول في التتارخانية : أخذ رجل ثوباً وقال اذهب به فإن رضيته اشتريته فذهب به وضاع الثوب فلا شيء عليه، ولو قال رضيته أخذته بعشرة فضاع فهو ضامن قيمته وفي النصاب وعليه الفتوى وهذا بناء على أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء إنما يكون مضموناً إذا كان الثمن مسمى .اهـ. وهذا بالقواعد أمس مما في فروق الكرابيسي من أنه في البحر الرائق ج٦ م٢
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option of Condition. The third: ten, and this twenty, and this thirty, so carry the garments to your home, whichever garment you are pleased with I have sold it to you. He carried them and they were destroyed in the possession of the buyer. The Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: If all are destroyed together or successively, and it is not known which was destroyed first and which after, the buyer is liable for one-third of each garment. If the first is known, that garment is incumbent on him, and the two garments are a trust with him. If the two garments were destroyed and the third remains, he returns the third because it is a trust, and as for the two garments, half the price of each is incumbent on him if he does not know which was destroyed first. If one was destroyed and two remain, the price of the destroyed one is incumbent on him and he returns the two garments. If the two garments were burned and the third decreased by one-third or one-fourth, and it is not known which was burned first, he returns what remains and is not liable for the decrease due to burning proportionally, and half the price of each of the two garments is incumbent on him. End. So this is explicit that the statement of the price by the seller is sufficient for liability. And in al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah: 'Take it, if I am pleased I will buy it' — he took it and it was lost, he is not liable. If he said: 'If I am pleased I will buy it for ten' and he took it and it was lost, he is liable. End. This is explicit in what we said. And the distinction between what is taken on negotiation for purchase and what is taken for the purpose of looking has been obscure to him. For in what he transmitted from al-Qunyah, it is only said: 'the negotiator until I look at it', and what is taken for looking is a trust. And what we mentioned from the authors of fatawa is only said: 'If I am pleased I will buy it'. The proof of the difference between them is that it is a cause like emancipation, for its cause is only kinship. So ponder his statement: (This is explicit in what we said). Al-Ramli said: The apparent is that this comes from the buyer, not the seller, so it is evidence against him, not for him. Yes, what preceded from al-Khaniyyah is explicit in what he said, so reflect. End. I said: Al-Tarsusi also transmitted from al-Khaniyyah: A man sold a commodity and said to another: look at it. He took it to look at it, and it was destroyed in his hand, he is not liable. If the looker said after looking: for how much are you selling? They said: he is liable. The correct is that he is not liable unless the owner of the commodity said: for such. End. And al-Tarsusi interpreted it as where the buyer also said: for such, to agree with the interpretation of their statements as not being satisfied with the statement of the price from the seller only. And this is far from what is in Sharh Nazm al-Kanz by the Allamah al-Maqdisi, that the author did not understand the intention of al-Tarsusi and therefore accused him of error. That is because he intended that it is necessary to specify the price from both sides, either actually or legally. As for the first, it is apparent. As for the second, it is by one of them specifying and the other issuing something that indicates satisfaction with it, as in his statement: 'Take it, if I take it for ten' — for his handing it over after his statement indicates satisfaction, unlike his statement: 'until I look', for he did not agree to what he specified but made it conditioned upon looking and turned away from what was specified. And all that they mentioned contains specification by one of them, and they ruled for liability in the second category upon reflection. And one who looks at the statement of al-Tarsusi finds it calling out to what we mentioned. End. I did not see in the statement of al-Tarsusi what calls out to what he mentioned; rather what he explicitly stated is that liability is when the seller and the negotiator in the state of negotiation mention a price, or the buyer alone mentions it. And he also said: If it were sufficient to mention the price from the seller alone, liability would have to apply in their statement: 'the owner of the garment said: it is for ten' or 'take it for ten' and the negotiator said: 'take it until I look at it' and he took it and it was lost and destroyed in his hand, that he is liable. And they have stated in all the books that it is on negotiation of liability what is in al-Khaniyyah: He said: If he took a garment on negotiation, and the seller handed it to him while he is negotiating and the seller says: it is for ten, then he is bound by the price that the seller said until the buyer rejects it. If he negotiated and the buyer said: 'until I look at it', and he handed it over and it was lost from him, then nothing is upon the buyer because he only took it for looking. And if he took it other than for looking, then said: 'until I look at it', his statement 'until I look at it' does not remove him from [liability]. End. So this is explicit in the difference between them. And in al-Dhakhirah, attributed to Abu Yusuf: A man negotiated with a man for a garment, and the owner of the garment said: it is for ten, and the negotiator said: 'take it until I look at it', and he handed it over to him on that, and it was lost, nothing is incumbent on him. He explained saying: because he took it for looking, indicating that this is not a possession of purchase. End. So this is explicit in the difference between them as well. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: A man said: this garment is yours for ten, and he said: 'take it until I look at it' or said: 'until I show it to someone else', and he took it on that and it was lost in his hand, he is not liable according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. If he said: 'take it, for if I am pleased I will take it' and it was lost, the price is upon him. End. This is also explicit. So it is established by these quotations from the relied-upon books that there is no difference in what is taken on negotiation for purchase between the statement of the price by the seller or by the buyer alone. And the seal of the verifiers, Ibn al-Humam, spoke truly in Fath al-Qadir when he said in the Book of Waqf: Indeed al-Tarsusi is far from fiqh. Then I saw the difference between them also explicitly in the Furq of al-Karabisi, from which I transmitted: He said: If he said: this garment is yours for ten, and he said: 'take it until I look at it' or 'until I show it to someone else', and he took it and it was lost, Abu Hanifah said: nothing upon him, meaning it is destroyed as a trust. If he said: 'take it until I look at it, for if I am pleased I will take it', and it was destroyed, then the price is upon him. The difference is that in the first case, he ordered him to look at it or show it to someone else, and that is not a sale. As for the other case, he ordered him to bring it so that he may be pleased with it and take it, and that is a sale without the order, so with the order it is more appropriate. End. And the apparent from their statements is that there is no difference between destruction or consumption. And what is in al-Dhakhirah from Abu Yusuf that what is taken on negotiation for purchase is liable for the price is carried upon the value. And what he mentioned: he is not liable, and they stated in all the cases in which the price is mentioned from the negotiator alone that he is liable. End. After this, the apparent is that the intent is what al-Maqdisi said, even if it is far from the statement of al-Tarsusi. That is because the specification if it is from the buyer is valid on the basis that the seller, when he handed over the sold item, became satisfied with it. Similarly, if it is from the seller and the buyer took it being satisfied with it. His statement: (As for the other case, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: And I say in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: A man took a garment and said: 'take it, for if I am pleased I will buy it', and he took it and the garment was lost, then nothing upon him. If he said: 'I am pleased, I took it for ten', and it was lost, then he is liable for its value. And in al-Nisab: and upon it is the fatwa. And this is based on the fact that what is taken on negotiation for purchase is only liable if the price is specified. End. And this is closer to the principles than what is in Furq al-Karabisi. End of Al-Bahr al-Raiq, volume 6, part 2.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Al-Bahr al-Raiq on the ruling of liability for goods taken on negotiation for purchase. The author first presents a case from the matn: if a buyer takes multiple garments to his home with an option to choose, and they are destroyed, Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl gives detailed rulings on the buyer's liability depending on whether the order of destruction is known. From this, the author extracts the principle that the seller's mention of the price alone is sufficient to make the taker liable. He then supports this by quoting from Al-Khulasah and Al-Bazzaziyyah, where two scenarios are contrasted: (1) if the buyer says 'take it, if I am pleased I will buy it' without mentioning a price, there is no liability; (2) if he says 'if I am pleased I will buy it for ten', there is liability. The author emphasizes that the distinction is between taking for negotiation (sawm al-shira') and taking for mere looking (wajh al-nazar). The former, when a price is mentioned, creates liability; the latter is a trust. The commentary then addresses a possible confusion by al-Ramli and al-Tarsusi, arguing that the correct Hanafi position is that mentioning the price by either party suffices. Numerous books are cited, including Al-Khaniyyah, Al-Dhakhirah, Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, and Furq al-Karabisi, all confirming that if the taker says 'hāt ḥattā anẓur' (take it so I may look), there is no liability, but if he says 'hāt fa-in raḍītuhu akhadhtuhu' (take it, and if I am pleased I will take it), he is liable even if only the seller mentioned the price. The author concludes that there is no difference whether the price is mentioned by the seller or buyer, and this is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
المقبوض على سوم الشراء (al-maqbūḍ 'alā sawm al-shirā'): Goods taken by a potential buyer during negotiation with the intention to purchase, where a price has been mentioned.
أمانة (amānah): A trust; goods held without liability for loss unless negligence occurs.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to pay the price or compensation for the goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, which type of possession makes the taker liable for the price?
A) Taking goods with the statement 'take it until I look at it' (hāt ḥattā anẓur) without price mention
B) Taking goods with the statement 'take it, if I am pleased I will buy it for ten' (hāt fa-in raḍītuhu akhadhtuhu bi-'asharah)
C) Taking goods as a gift
D) Taking goods on a loan basis

Key Takeaway
Mentioning the price by either party (seller or buyer) is sufficient to make the taker on negotiation liable for the goods if they are destroyed.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Liability for Goods Taken on Bargaining: Inspection vs Purchase
Explaining the ruling of daman for goods taken on bargaining with price specified by either party.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between taking goods for inspection (trust, no liability) and taking them with intention to purchase (sale, liability for price/value) in the context of musawama.

Core Idea
Goods taken for inspection are a trust; goods taken for purchase are a sale with liability.

When you take an item from a seller to examine it, you are not yet a buyer. But if you take it with the words 'if I like it, I'll take it', the transaction becomes a sale. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on liability (daman) for goods taken on bargaining (sawm al-shira) and the crucial role of the taker's intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two distinct phrases: 'give it to me until I look at it' (inspection) vs 'give it to me, if I am pleased I will take it' (purchase intent).
The wording is decisive for the ruling.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For inspection: no liability (amanah). For purchase intent: liable for price/value upon loss or consumption.
The sources use 'no thing upon him' vs 'the price is upon him'.
3
Examine the evidence from authoritative texts
The author cites al-Khaniyya, al-Dhakhira, and Fatawa al-Dhahiriyya to establish the difference.
These are reliable Hanafi sources (zahir riwayah).
4
Understand the rationale
The first scenario is not a sale; possession is a trust. The second scenario is a sale because the taker's words indicate a commitment.
The seller's delivery in the second case is part of the sale.
5
Apply to a new example
If a buyer says 'let me take it home to show my wife' without promising purchase, it is inspection. If he says 'I'll take it if she approves', it is purchase intent.
The ruling remains the same even if the price is mentioned.

الضمان
ما في الخانية قال : ولو أخذ ثوباً على المساومة فدفعه إليه البائع وهو يساومه والبائع يقول هو بعشرة فهو على الثمن الذي قال البائع حتى يرد عليه المشتري، وإن ساومه فقال المشتري حتى أنظر إليه فدفعه فضاع منه فليس على المشتري شيء لأنه إنما أخذه للنظر، وإن أخذه على غير النظر ثم قال حتى انظر إله فقوله حتى أنظر إليه لا يخرجه عن اهـ. فهذا صريح في الفرق بينهما وفي الذخيرة معزياً لأبي يوسف: رجل ساوم رجلاً بثوب فقال صاحب الثوب هو بعشرة فقال المساوم هاته حتى أنظر إليه فدفعه إليه على ذلك فضاع لا يلزمه شيء. علل فقال : لأنه أخذه على النظر إشارة إلى أن هذا ليس بمقبوض الشراء اهـ. فهذا صريح في الفرق بينهما أيضاً. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية: رجل قال هذا الثوب لك بعشرة فقال هاته حتى أنظر إليه أو قال حتى أريه غيري فأخذه على ذلك فضاع في يده لم يضمن في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ولو قال هاته فإن رضيته أخذته فضاع كان عليه الثمن اهـ. وهذا صريح أيضاً فثبت بهذه النقول من الكتب المعتمدة أنه لا فرق في المقبوض على سوم الشراء بين بيان الثمن من البائع أو من المشتري وحده، ولقد صدق ختام المحققين ابن الهمام في فتح القدير حيث قال في كتاب الوقف : إن الطرسوسي بعيد عن الفقه، ثم رأيت الفرق بينهما أيضاً صريحاً في فروق الكرابيسي ومنها نقلت قال : لو قال هذا الثوب لك بعشرة فقال هاته حتى أنظر إليه أو حتى أريه غيري فأخذه فضاع قال أبو حنيفة : لا شيء عليه يعني يهلك أمانة وإن قال هاته حتى أنظر إليه فإن رضيته أخذته فهلك فعليه الثمن. والفرق أن في الفصل الأول أمره لينظر إليه أو ليريه غيره وذلك ليس ببيع، فأما في الفصل الآخر أمره بالإتيان به ليرضاه ويأخذه وذلك بيع بدون الأمر فمع الأمر أولى اهـ.
والظاهر من كلامهم أنه لا فرق بين الهلاك أو الاستهلاك، وما في الذخيرة عن أبي يوسف أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء مضمون بالثمن محمول على القيمة، وما ذكره
لا يضمن ونصوا في جميع الصور التي فيها ذكر الثمن من جهة المساوم وحده أنه يضمن اهـ. وبعد هذا فالظاهر أن المراد هو ما قاله المقدسي وإن كان بعيداً من كلام الطرسوسي وذلك أن التسمية إذا كانت من المشتري تصح باعتبار أن البائع لما سلمه المبيع صار راضياً بها فكذا إذا كانت من البائع و قبضه المشتري راضياً بها .
قوله : (فأما في الفصل الآخر الخ) قال في النهر وأقول في التتارخانية : أخذ رجل ثوباً وقال اذهب به فإن رضيته اشتريته فذهب به وضاع الثوب فلا شيء عليه، ولو قال رضيته أخذته بعشرة فضاع فهو ضامن قيمته وفي النصاب وعليه الفتوى وهذا بناء على أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء إنما يكون مضموناً إذا كان الثمن مسمى .اهـ. وهذا بالقواعد أمس مما في فروق الكرابيسي من أنه في
الطرسوسي من أنه إن هلك فمضمون بالقيمة وإن استهلكه فمضمون بالثمن ليس بصحيح لما في الخانية : إذا أخذ ثوباً على وجه المساومة بعد بيان الثمن فهلك في يده كان عليه قيمته، وكذا لو استهلكه وارث المشتري بعد موت المشتري .اهـ. والوارث كالمورث، وأما مقبوض الوكيل بالسوم فقال في الخانية : الوكيل بالشراء إذا أخذ الثوب على سوم الشراء فأراه الموكل ولم يرض به ورده عليه فهلك عند الوكيل قال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل: ضمن الوكيل قيمته ولا يرجع بها على الموكل إلا أن يأمره الوكيل بالأخذ على سوم الشراء فحينئذ إذا ضمن الوكيل رجع على الموكل اهـ. وفي البزازية : غلط وسلم غير المبيع وهلك ضمن القيمة لأنه قبضه على جهة البيع بعث رسولاً إلى البزاز وقال ابعث إلي ثوب كذا فبعث إليه البزاز معه أو مع غيره فضاع الثوب قبل الوصول إلى الآمر وتصادقوا عليه لا ضمان على الرسول، ثم إن كان رسول الآمر فالضمان على الآمر، وإن كان رسول البزاز فلا ضمان على أحد لكن إذا وصل إلى الآمر ضمن الآمر ، وكذا لو أرسل إلى آخر وقال أرسل إلي عشرة دراهم قرضاً فأرسل فالآمر ضامن إذا أقر أنه رسوله، فإن بعثه مع غير رسوله لا ضمان على الآمر قبل أن يصل، وكذا الدائن إذا بعث رسولاً لقبض دينه
رسي
معه
الثاني يكون بيعاً .اهـ. قوله : (ليس بصحيح لما في الخانية الخ قال في النهر : لا نسلم أنه غير صحيح إذ الطرسوس لم يذكره تفقهاً بل نقلاً . عن المشايخ صرح به في المنتقى وعلله في المحيط بأنه صار راضياً بالمبيع دلالة حملاً لقوله على الصلاح والسداد، وعزاه في الخزانة أيضاً إلى المنتقى غير أنه قال: وفي القياس تجب القيمة قال الطرسوسي : وينبغي أن لا يزاد بها على المسمى كما في الإجارة الفاسدة وفيه نظر، بل ينبغي أن تجب القيمة بالغة وقد صرحوا بذلك في البيع الفاسد فكذا هذا. اهـ كلام النهر . قلت : ولا يرد ما نقله المؤلف عن الخانية لأن المساوم إذا استهلك الثوب يكون راضياً بالثمن المذكور فصح البيع بالثمن بخلاف استهلاك وارثه لأن الوارث غير عاقد فقول المؤلف والوارث كالمورث ممنوع يؤيده ما ذكره الطرسوسي عن المنتقى لو قال لآخر خذ هذا الثوب بعشرين فقال المشتري آخذه بعشرة فذهب بالثوب وهلكه في يده فعليه قيمته لأنه قبضه بجهة البيع وقد ثمناً، ولو استهلكه فعليه عشرون لأنه بالاستهلاك صار البيع بالمسمى دلالة حملاً لفعله على الصلاح والسداد. ولو قال البائع رجعت عما قلت أو مات أحدهما قبل أن يقول المشتري رضيت انتقض جهة البيع فإن استهلكه المشتري بعد ذلك فعليه قيمته كما في حقيقة البيع لو انتقض يبقى المبيع في يده مضموناً فكذا هنا اهـ. فحيث انتقض البيع فكيف يكون الوارث كالمورث لأن العقد صدر بين البائع والمورث وقد انتقض البيع بموته فيكون المبيع محض أمانة في يد الوارث، فإذا استهلكه يلزمه قيمته بخلاف استهلاك المورث لأنه يكون رضا بإمضاء العقد، ويفهم هذا من قول الخانية : وكذا لو استهلكه وارث المشتري الخ . فإنه يفيد أن المورث لو استهلكه لا يكون كاستهلاك الوارث بل يلزمه الثمن لما قلنا .
بین
له
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option of Stipulation. On the subject of bargaining and liability. In al-Khaniyya: If someone took a cloth on bargaining and the seller gave it to him while he was bargaining and the seller said it is for ten, then it is on the price stated by the seller until the buyer returns it. And if he bargained and the buyer said 'until I look at it' and he gave it and it was lost, then nothing is on the buyer because he only took it for looking. And if he took it without looking then said 'until I look at it', his saying 'until I look at it' does not remove it from [liability]. So this is explicit in the difference between them. And in al-Dhakhira attributed to Abu Yusuf: A man bargained with another for a cloth, and the owner said it is for ten, and the bargainer said 'give it to me until I look at it' and he gave it on that condition and it was lost, nothing is required of him. He gave the reason: because he took it for looking, indicating that this is not a captured-for-purchase. So this is also explicit in the difference. And in Fatawa al-Dhahiriyya: A man said 'this cloth is yours for ten', and he said 'give it to me until I look at it' or 'until I show it to someone else', and he took it on that condition and it was lost in his hand, he is not liable according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And if he said 'give it to me, for if I am pleased with it I will take it' and it was lost, then the price is upon him. So this is also explicit. Thus it is established by these quotations from reliable books that there is no difference in the captured-on-bargaining between the statement of the price by the seller or by the buyer alone. And indeed the seal of the investigators Ibn al-Humam spoke truth in Fath al-Qadir where he said in the Book of Waqf: al-Tarsusi is far from fiqh. Then I saw the difference between them also explicitly in Furuq al-Karabisi, from which I quoted: He said: If he said 'this cloth is yours for ten' and he said 'give it to me until I look at it' or 'until I show it to someone else' and he took it and it was lost, Abu Hanifa said: nothing upon him, meaning it is destroyed as a trust. And if he said 'give it to me until I look at it, for if I am pleased with it I will take it' and it was lost, then the price is upon him. The difference is that in the first case he ordered him to look at it or show it to someone else, and that is not a sale. As for the other case, he ordered him to bring it so that he may be pleased with it and take it, and that is a sale without the order, so with the order it is more appropriate. It is apparent from their statements that there is no difference between destruction or consumption. And what is in al-Dhakhira from Abu Yusuf that the captured-on-bargaining is liable with the price is interpreted as with the value. And what he mentioned is not liable, and they stated in all the cases where the price is mentioned by the bargainer alone that he is liable. After this, it is apparent that the intended meaning is what al-Maqdisi said, even if it is far from the statement of al-Tarsusi: that the specification when it is from the buyer is valid because the seller, when he handed over the sold item, became satisfied with it, so likewise when it is from the seller and the buyer took it being satisfied with it. His statement: (As for the other chapter, etc.) said in al-Nahr: And I say in al-Tatarakhaniyya: A man took a cloth and said 'go with it, and if I am pleased with it I will buy it' so he went with it and the cloth was lost, nothing upon him. And if he said 'if I am pleased with it I will take it for ten' and it was lost, he is liable for its value. And in al-Nisab the fatwa is upon this, and this is based on the captured-on-bargaining being liable only if the price is specified. This is more in accordance with the rules than what is in Furuq al-Karabisi that in al-Tarsusi: if it is destroyed, liable with the value; if he consumes it, liable with the price is not correct because in al-Khaniyya: if he took a cloth on the basis of bargaining after the statement of the price and it was destroyed in his hand, he owes its value, and likewise if his heir consumed it after the death of the purchaser. And the heir is like the deceased. As for the captured-by-agent on bargaining, it is said in al-Khaniyya: The agent for purchase if he took the cloth on bargaining and showed it to the principal and he did not approve and returned it to him, and it was destroyed with the agent, the shaykh imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: the agent is liable for its value and he cannot recover it from the principal unless the agent ordered him to take on bargaining, then if the agent is liable he recovers from the principal. And in al-Bazzaziyya: He made a mistake and delivered other than the sold item and it was destroyed, he is liable for the value because he took it on the basis of sale. He sent a messenger to the cloth merchant and said 'send me such and such cloth' so the cloth merchant sent it with him or with someone else and the cloth was lost before reaching the orderer and they agreed on it: no liability on the messenger. Then if he is the messenger of the orderer, the liability is on the orderer; if he is the messenger of the cloth merchant, no liability on anyone, but if it reaches the orderer, the orderer is liable. Likewise if he sent to someone else and said 'send me ten dirhams as a loan' and he sent, the orderer is liable if he acknowledges that he is his messenger. If he sent with other than his messenger, no liability on the orderer before it reaches. Likewise the creditor if he sends a messenger to collect his debt. [unclear words]. The second is a sale. His statement: (Not correct because in al-Khaniyya) said in al-Nahr: We do not accept that it is incorrect because al-Tarsusi did not mention it as a juristic deduction but as a transmission from the shaykhs. It is stated explicitly in al-Muntaqa and explained in al-Muhit that he becomes satisfied with the sold item as an indication, interpreting his statement as for goodness and correctness. And he attributed it in al-Khazana also to al-Muntaqa except that he said: In qiyas the value is obligatory. Al-Tarsusi said: It should not exceed the named amount as in invalid hire, but there is consideration; rather the value in full should be obligatory as they stated in invalid sale, so also here. This is the statement of al-Nahr. I say: What the author quoted from al-Khaniyya does not refute because the bargainer if he consumes the cloth becomes satisfied with the mentioned price, so the sale with the price is valid, unlike the consumption of his heir because the heir is not a contractor. So the author's statement 'the heir is like the deceased' is not accepted, supported by what al-Tarsusi mentioned from al-Muntaqa: If he said to another 'take this cloth for twenty' and the buyer said 'I will take it for ten' and he took the cloth and destroyed it in his hand, he owes its value because he took it on the basis of sale and they have priced it. And if he consumed it, he owes twenty because by consumption the sale becomes the named price as an indication, interpreting his action as for goodness and correctness. And if the seller said 'I retract my statement' or one of them died before the buyer said 'I am pleased', the basis of sale is rescinded. If the buyer consumes it after that, he owes its value as in the reality of a sale if it is rescinded, the sold item remains in his hand as a guarantee, so also here. So when the sale is rescinded, how can the heir be like the deceased? Because the contract occurred between the seller and the deceased and the sale was rescinded by his death, so the sold item becomes a pure trust in the hand of the heir. So if he consumes it, he owes its value, unlike the consumption of the deceased because it is satisfaction with executing the contract. And this is understood from the statement of al-Khaniyya: 'And likewise if the heir of the purchaser consumed it' etc. It indicates that if the deceased consumed it, it is not like the consumption of the heir; rather he owes the price for what we said Between? For him?
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling regarding goods taken on the basis of bargaining (sawm al-shira) and the liability (daman) when the price is specified by either the seller or the buyer. The author begins by citing multiple authoritative sources to establish the general rule: if a person takes a cloth on musawama (bargaining) for inspection, and it is lost, there is no liability because it was taken as a trust (amanah). However, if the taker explicitly states that he will take it upon approval, the goods become a sale, and he is liable for the price or value upon loss. The key distinction is the intention and wording of the taker. The passage then addresses an apparent dispute: some earlier scholars, like al-Tarsusi, suggested a difference between the price being specified by the seller or by the buyer. The author refutes this, citing numerous authorities that there is no difference—both cases result in liability if the goods were taken for purchase. The commentary then delves into the distinction between loss (hulak) and consumption (istihlak), critiquing al-Tarsusi's view that consumption incurs price while loss incurs value. The author argues that the relied-upon position is that consumption by the original taker establishes the sale at the named price, while consumption by the heir does not, because the heir is not a party to the contract. The passage also covers cases involving agents and messengers, emphasizing that liability depends on whose agent the taker is and the terms of possession. Overall, the author clarifies the Hanafi position with rigorous rationalist reasoning (istihsan) and textual support from the mutun and shuruh.

Key Terms
المقبوض على سوم الشراء (al-maqbud 'ala sawm al-shira): Goods taken by a potential buyer on the basis of bargaining or negotiation for purchase, where the price may or may not be specified.
المساومة (al-musawama): Bargaining or negotiating a price without a final commitment to purchase.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or damage of goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi sources cited, what is the ruling on a person who takes a cloth saying 'give it to me until I look at it' and it is lost?
A) He is liable for the price.
B) He is liable for the value.
C) He is not liable because it was taken as a trust for inspection.
D) He is liable only if the price was stated by the seller.

Key Takeaway
The liability for goods taken on bargaining depends on the taker's wording: inspection wording yields no liability; purchase intent wording yields liability.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
The Internal Hanafi Dispute: Does It Matter Who Specifies the Price?
Refuting al-Tarsusi's distinction and detailing liability on destruction vs consumption.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi majority rejects al-Tarsusi's distinction between seller-specified and buyer-specified prices, and state the correct ruling for consumption vs loss.

Core Idea
The ruling does not change based on who names the price; intention rules. Consumption by the original taker establishes the sale; consumption by the heir does not.

While the basic ruling is clear, some Hanafi scholars like al-Tarsusi proposed a nuance: if the seller specifies the price, the liability is for value, but if the buyer specifies, it is for the named price. The author, with backing from Ibn al-Humam and other major authorities, firmly rejects this. This lesson explores that internal dispute and the finer details of liability when goods are consumed versus lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Tarsusi's position
Al-Tarsusi reportedly held that if the seller states the price, the taker is liable for value upon loss; if the buyer states the price, the taker is liable for the named price.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference, not between madhahib.
2
Examine the Hanafi majority response
The author and Ibn al-Humam reject this, citing multiple authoritative texts showing no distinction based on who specifies the price.
The decisive factor is the taker's wording, not the price specifier.
3
Understand the distinction between loss and consumption
If the taker consumes the goods, he becomes satisfied with the named price, establishing a sale. Loss (without consumption) incurs liability for value.
The heir's consumption does not create a sale because the heir is not a party to the original contract.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario with an heir
If the original taker dies and the goods are with his heir, the possession becomes a pure trust. If the heir consumes, he owes value, not the price.
The contract was rescinded by death; the heir's consumption does not indicate satisfaction with the price.

كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط
على سوم
الضمان
ما في الخانية قال : ولو أخذ ثوباً على المساومة فدفعه إليه البائع وهو يساومه والبائع يقول هو بعشرة فهو على الثمن الذي قال البائع حتى يرد عليه المشتري، وإن ساومه فقال المشتري حتى أنظر إليه فدفعه فضاع منه فليس على المشتري شيء لأنه إنما أخذه للنظر، وإن أخذه على غير النظر ثم قال حتى انظر إله فقوله حتى أنظر إليه لا يخرجه عن اهـ. فهذا صريح في الفرق بينهما وفي الذخيرة معزياً لأبي يوسف: رجل ساوم رجلاً بثوب فقال صاحب الثوب هو بعشرة فقال المساوم هاته حتى أنظر إليه فدفعه إليه على ذلك فضاع لا يلزمه شيء. علل فقال : لأنه أخذه على النظر إشارة إلى أن هذا ليس بمقبوض الشراء اهـ. فهذا صريح في الفرق بينهما أيضاً. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية: رجل قال هذا الثوب لك بعشرة فقال هاته حتى أنظر إليه أو قال حتى أريه غيري فأخذه على ذلك فضاع في يده لم يضمن في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ولو قال هاته فإن رضيته أخذته فضاع كان عليه الثمن اهـ. وهذا صريح أيضاً فثبت بهذه النقول من الكتب المعتمدة أنه لا فرق في المقبوض على سوم الشراء بين بيان الثمن من البائع أو من المشتري وحده، ولقد صدق ختام المحققين ابن الهمام في فتح القدير حيث قال في كتاب الوقف : إن الطرسوسي بعيد عن الفقه، ثم رأيت الفرق بينهما أيضاً صريحاً في فروق الكرابيسي ومنها نقلت قال : لو قال هذا الثوب لك بعشرة فقال هاته حتى أنظر إليه أو حتى أريه غيري فأخذه فضاع قال أبو حنيفة : لا شيء عليه يعني يهلك أمانة وإن قال هاته حتى أنظر إليه فإن رضيته أخذته فهلك فعليه الثمن. والفرق أن في الفصل الأول أمره لينظر إليه أو ليريه غيره وذلك ليس ببيع، فأما في الفصل الآخر أمره بالإتيان به ليرضاه ويأخذه وذلك بيع بدون الأمر فمع الأمر أولى اهـ.
والظاهر من كلامهم أنه لا فرق بين الهلاك أو الاستهلاك، وما في الذخيرة عن أبي يوسف أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء مضمون بالثمن محمول على القيمة، وما ذكره
لا يضمن ونصوا في جميع الصور التي فيها ذكر الثمن من جهة المساوم وحده أنه يضمن اهـ. وبعد هذا فالظاهر أن المراد هو ما قاله المقدسي وإن كان بعيداً من كلام الطرسوسي وذلك أن التسمية إذا كانت من المشتري تصح باعتبار أن البائع لما سلمه المبيع صار راضياً بها فكذا إذا كانت من البائع و قبضه المشتري راضياً بها .
قوله : (فأما في الفصل الآخر الخ) قال في النهر وأقول في التتارخانية : أخذ رجل ثوباً وقال اذهب به فإن رضيته اشتريته فذهب به وضاع الثوب فلا شيء عليه، ولو قال رضيته أخذته بعشرة فضاع فهو ضامن قيمته وفي النصاب وعليه الفتوى وهذا بناء على أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء إنما يكون مضموناً إذا كان الثمن مسمى .اهـ. وهذا بالقواعد أمس مما في فروق الكرابيسي من أنه في
الطرسوسي من أنه إن هلك فمضمون بالقيمة وإن استهلكه فمضمون بالثمن ليس بصحيح لما في الخانية : إذا أخذ ثوباً على وجه المساومة بعد بيان الثمن فهلك في يده كان عليه قيمته، وكذا لو استهلكه وارث المشتري بعد موت المشتري .اهـ. والوارث كالمورث، وأما مقبوض الوكيل بالسوم فقال في الخانية : الوكيل بالشراء إذا أخذ الثوب على سوم الشراء فأراه الموكل ولم يرض به ورده عليه فهلك عند الوكيل قال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل: ضمن الوكيل قيمته ولا يرجع بها على الموكل إلا أن يأمره الوكيل بالأخذ على سوم الشراء فحينئذ إذا ضمن الوكيل رجع على الموكل اهـ. وفي البزازية : غلط وسلم غير المبيع وهلك ضمن القيمة لأنه قبضه على جهة البيع بعث رسولاً إلى البزاز وقال ابعث إلي ثوب كذا فبعث إليه البزاز معه أو مع غيره فضاع الثوب قبل الوصول إلى الآمر وتصادقوا عليه لا ضمان على الرسول، ثم إن كان رسول الآمر فالضمان على الآمر، وإن كان رسول البزاز فلا ضمان على أحد لكن إذا وصل إلى الآمر ضمن الآمر ، وكذا لو أرسل إلى آخر وقال أرسل إلي عشرة دراهم قرضاً فأرسل فالآمر ضامن إذا أقر أنه رسوله، فإن بعثه مع غير رسوله لا ضمان على الآمر قبل أن يصل، وكذا الدائن إذا بعث رسولاً لقبض دينه

معه
الثاني يكون بيعاً .اهـ. قوله : (ليس بصحيح لما في الخانية الخ قال في النهر : لا نسلم أنه غير صحيح إذ الطرسوس لم يذكره تفقهاً بل نقلاً . عن المشايخ صرح به في المنتقى وعلله في المحيط بأنه صار راضياً بالمبيع دلالة حملاً لقوله على الصلاح والسداد، وعزاه في الخزانة أيضاً إلى المنتقى غير أنه قال: وفي القياس تجب القيمة قال الطرسوسي : وينبغي أن لا يزاد بها على المسمى كما في الإجارة الفاسدة وفيه نظر، بل ينبغي أن تجب القيمة بالغة وقد صرحوا بذلك في البيع الفاسد فكذا هذا. اهـ كلام النهر . قلت : ولا يرد ما نقله المؤلف عن الخانية لأن المساوم إذا استهلك الثوب يكون راضياً بالثمن المذكور فصح البيع بالثمن بخلاف استهلاك وارثه لأن الوارث غير عاقد فقول المؤلف والوارث كالمورث ممنوع يؤيده ما ذكره الطرسوسي عن المنتقى لو قال لآخر خذ هذا الثوب بعشرين فقال المشتري آخذه بعشرة فذهب بالثوب وهلكه في يده فعليه قيمته لأنه قبضه بجهة البيع وقد ثمناً، ولو استهلكه فعليه عشرون لأنه بالاستهلاك صار البيع بالمسمى دلالة حملاً لفعله على الصلاح والسداد. ولو قال البائع رجعت عما قلت أو مات أحدهما قبل أن يقول المشتري رضيت انتقض جهة البيع فإن استهلكه المشتري بعد ذلك فعليه قيمته كما في حقيقة البيع لو انتقض يبقى المبيع في يده مضموناً فكذا هنا اهـ. فحيث انتقض البيع فكيف يكون الوارث كالمورث لأن العقد صدر بين البائع والمورث وقد انتقض البيع بموته فيكون المبيع محض أمانة في يد الوارث، فإذا استهلكه يلزمه قيمته بخلاف استهلاك المورث لأنه يكون رضا بإمضاء العقد، ويفهم هذا من قول الخانية : وكذا لو استهلكه وارث المشتري الخ . فإنه يفيد أن المورث لو استهلكه لا يكون كاستهلاك الوارث بل يلزمه الثمن لما قلنا .
بین
له
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option of Stipulation. On the subject of bargaining and liability. In al-Khaniyya: If someone took a cloth on bargaining and the seller gave it to him while he was bargaining and the seller said it is for ten, then it is on the price stated by the seller until the buyer returns it. And if he bargained and the buyer said 'until I look at it' and he gave it and it was lost, then nothing is on the buyer because he only took it for looking. And if he took it without looking then said 'until I look at it', his saying 'until I look at it' does not remove it from [liability]. So this is explicit in the difference between them. And in al-Dhakhira attributed to Abu Yusuf: A man bargained with another for a cloth, and the owner said it is for ten, and the bargainer said 'give it to me until I look at it' and he gave it on that condition and it was lost, nothing is required of him. He gave the reason: because he took it for looking, indicating that this is not a captured-for-purchase. So this is also explicit in the difference. And in Fatawa al-Dhahiriyya: A man said 'this cloth is yours for ten', and he said 'give it to me until I look at it' or 'until I show it to someone else', and he took it on that condition and it was lost in his hand, he is not liable according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And if he said 'give it to me, for if I am pleased with it I will take it' and it was lost, then the price is upon him. So this is also explicit. Thus it is established by these quotations from reliable books that there is no difference in the captured-on-bargaining between the statement of the price by the seller or by the buyer alone. And indeed the seal of the investigators Ibn al-Humam spoke truth in Fath al-Qadir where he said in the Book of Waqf: al-Tarsusi is far from fiqh. Then I saw the difference between them also explicitly in Furuq al-Karabisi, from which I quoted: He said: If he said 'this cloth is yours for ten' and he said 'give it to me until I look at it' or 'until I show it to someone else' and he took it and it was lost, Abu Hanifa said: nothing upon him, meaning it is destroyed as a trust. And if he said 'give it to me until I look at it, for if I am pleased with it I will take it' and it was lost, then the price is upon him. The difference is that in the first case he ordered him to look at it or show it to someone else, and that is not a sale. As for the other case, he ordered him to bring it so that he may be pleased with it and take it, and that is a sale without the order, so with the order it is more appropriate. It is apparent from their statements that there is no difference between destruction or consumption. And what is in al-Dhakhira from Abu Yusuf that the captured-on-bargaining is liable with the price is interpreted as with the value. And what he mentioned is not liable, and they stated in all the cases where the price is mentioned by the bargainer alone that he is liable. After this, it is apparent that the intended meaning is what al-Maqdisi said, even if it is far from the statement of al-Tarsusi: that the specification when it is from the buyer is valid because the seller, when he handed over the sold item, became satisfied with it, so likewise when it is from the seller and the buyer took it being satisfied with it. His statement: (As for the other chapter, etc.) said in al-Nahr: And I say in al-Tatarakhaniyya: A man took a cloth and said 'go with it, and if I am pleased with it I will buy it' so he went with it and the cloth was lost, nothing upon him. And if he said 'if I am pleased with it I will take it for ten' and it was lost, he is liable for its value. And in al-Nisab the fatwa is upon this, and this is based on the captured-on-bargaining being liable only if the price is specified. This is more in accordance with the rules than what is in Furuq al-Karabisi that in al-Tarsusi: if it is destroyed, liable with the value; if he consumes it, liable with the price is not correct because in al-Khaniyya: if he took a cloth on the basis of bargaining after the statement of the price and it was destroyed in his hand, he owes its value, and likewise if his heir consumed it after the death of the purchaser. And the heir is like the deceased. As for the captured-by-agent on bargaining, it is said in al-Khaniyya: The agent for purchase if he took the cloth on bargaining and showed it to the principal and he did not approve and returned it to him, and it was destroyed with the agent, the shaykh imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: the agent is liable for its value and he cannot recover it from the principal unless the agent ordered him to take on bargaining, then if the agent is liable he recovers from the principal. And in al-Bazzaziyya: He made a mistake and delivered other than the sold item and it was destroyed, he is liable for the value because he took it on the basis of sale. He sent a messenger to the cloth merchant and said 'send me such and such cloth' so the cloth merchant sent it with him or with someone else and the cloth was lost before reaching the orderer and they agreed on it: no liability on the messenger. Then if he is the messenger of the orderer, the liability is on the orderer; if he is the messenger of the cloth merchant, no liability on anyone, but if it reaches the orderer, the orderer is liable. Likewise if he sent to someone else and said 'send me ten dirhams as a loan' and he sent, the orderer is liable if he acknowledges that he is his messenger. If he sent with other than his messenger, no liability on the orderer before it reaches. Likewise the creditor if he sends a messenger to collect his debt. [unclear words]. The second is a sale. His statement: (Not correct because in al-Khaniyya) said in al-Nahr: We do not accept that it is incorrect because al-Tarsusi did not mention it as a juristic deduction but as a transmission from the shaykhs. It is stated explicitly in al-Muntaqa and explained in al-Muhit that he becomes satisfied with the sold item as an indication, interpreting his statement as for goodness and correctness. And he attributed it in al-Khazana also to al-Muntaqa except that he said: In qiyas the value is obligatory. Al-Tarsusi said: It should not exceed the named amount as in invalid hire, but there is consideration; rather the value in full should be obligatory as they stated in invalid sale, so also here. This is the statement of al-Nahr. I say: What the author quoted from al-Khaniyya does not refute because the bargainer if he consumes the cloth becomes satisfied with the mentioned price, so the sale with the price is valid, unlike the consumption of his heir because the heir is not a contractor. So the author's statement 'the heir is like the deceased' is not accepted, supported by what al-Tarsusi mentioned from al-Muntaqa: If he said to another 'take this cloth for twenty' and the buyer said 'I will take it for ten' and he took the cloth and destroyed it in his hand, he owes its value because he took it on the basis of sale and they have priced it. And if he consumed it, he owes twenty because by consumption the sale becomes the named price as an indication, interpreting his action as for goodness and correctness. And if the seller said 'I retract my statement' or one of them died before the buyer said 'I am pleased', the basis of sale is rescinded. If the buyer consumes it after that, he owes its value as in the reality of a sale if it is rescinded, the sold item remains in his hand as a guarantee, so also here. So when the sale is rescinded, how can the heir be like the deceased? Because the contract occurred between the seller and the deceased and the sale was rescinded by his death, so the sold item becomes a pure trust in the hand of the heir. So if he consumes it, he owes its value, unlike the consumption of the deceased because it is satisfaction with executing the contract. And this is understood from the statement of al-Khaniyya: 'And likewise if the heir of the purchaser consumed it' etc. It indicates that if the deceased consumed it, it is not like the consumption of the heir; rather he owes the price for what we said Between? For him?
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling regarding goods taken on the basis of bargaining (sawm al-shira) and the liability (daman) when the price is specified by either the seller or the buyer. The author begins by citing multiple authoritative sources to establish the general rule: if a person takes a cloth on musawama (bargaining) for inspection, and it is lost, there is no liability because it was taken as a trust (amanah). However, if the taker explicitly states that he will take it upon approval, the goods become a sale, and he is liable for the price or value upon loss. The key distinction is the intention and wording of the taker. The passage then addresses an apparent dispute: some earlier scholars, like al-Tarsusi, suggested a difference between the price being specified by the seller or by the buyer. The author refutes this, citing numerous authorities that there is no difference—both cases result in liability if the goods were taken for purchase. The commentary then delves into the distinction between loss (hulak) and consumption (istihlak), critiquing al-Tarsusi's view that consumption incurs price while loss incurs value. The author argues that the relied-upon position is that consumption by the original taker establishes the sale at the named price, while consumption by the heir does not, because the heir is not a party to the contract. The passage also covers cases involving agents and messengers, emphasizing that liability depends on whose agent the taker is and the terms of possession. Overall, the author clarifies the Hanafi position with rigorous rationalist reasoning (istihsan) and textual support from the mutun and shuruh.

Key Terms
الطرسوسي (al-Tarsusi): A Hanafi scholar who held a distinctive view on liability for goods taken on bargaining, differentiating based on who specified the price.
الهلاك (al-halāk): Destruction or loss of the goods without consumption by the taker.
الاستهلاك (al-istihlāk): Consumption of the goods by the taker, which indicates satisfaction with the named price and finalizes the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, if a buyer takes goods on bargaining and the price is specified by the seller, what is the liability if the goods are lost?
A) The buyer pays the named price.
B) The buyer pays the value of the goods.
C) The buyer pays nothing.
D) The buyer pays half the value.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority rejects any distinction based on who specifies the price; liability is determined by the taker's intention and whether the goods are lost or consumed.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
The Liability for Goods Taken for Bargaining: Refuting al-Tarsusi's View
Refutation of al-Tarsusi's view on liability for goods taken for bargaining

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on liability for goods taken for bargaining, distinguish between consumption by the buyer and by the heir, and apply the rule to a scenario involving a buyer or heir.

Core Idea
Consumption by the buyer confirms the sale at the named price; perishing or consumption by the heir requires market value.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding goods taken for bargaining (سوم الشراء). The issue is whether the liability for such goods when perished or consumed is based on the market value or the named price. The majority Hanafi position, supported by texts from al-Khaniyyah and al-Muntaqa, distinguishes between consumption by the buyer (which implies consent and binds the sale at the agreed price) and consumption by the heir or mere perishing (which triggers liability for market value). Al-Tarsusi proposed a different view, and the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refutes it by citing authoritative sources.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the core ruling: goods taken for bargaining are a trust until consumed. Consumption by the buyer makes the sale binding at the named price; perishing or consumption by the heir requires payment of market value.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view of al-Tarsusi
Al-Tarsusi held that both perishing and consumption lead to liability for the market value, or at least not exceeding the named price. Understand his reasoning: he considered consumption analogous to perishing, limiting liability to value.
Al-Tarsusi's view is based on transmission from some earlier scholars, but the majority disagree.
3
Analyze the evidence from al-Khaniyyah
The author cites al-Khaniyyah: if the buyer consumes, he pays the price; if the heir consumes, he pays the value. This supports the distinction. Also, the agent's liability is explained: if the agent consumes, he is liable for the value unless the principal authorized the bargaining.
These examples reinforce the principle that consumption by a contracting party implies consent.
4
Explain the distinction between buyer and heir
The buyer's consumption indicates acceptance of the sale, so the contract is concluded. The heir is not a party to the contract; the sale is nullified upon the buyer's death, so the goods become a trust in the heir's hands. Hence, consumption by the heir requires value, not price.
This is the key legal rationale (ta'lil).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that the buyer pays the named price if he consumes; otherwise, market value. This applies in fatwa and practice. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the seller receives the agreed price or market value.
This tarjih is supported by Ibn Nujaym and the majority.

Al-Tarsusi [stated] that if [the item] perishes, it is liable for its value, but if he consumes it, it is liable for the price. This is not correct, because in al-Khaniyyah: If he took a garment by way of bargaining after stating the price, and it perished in his hand, he must pay its value; likewise if the heir of the purchaser consumed it after the death of the purchaser. End quote. And the heir is like the inheritor. As for what is held by the agent for bargaining, it is said in al-Khaniyyah: The agent for purchase, if he took the garment for bargaining and showed it to the principal who was not satisfied and returned it to him, and it perished with the agent, the scholar Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: The agent is liable for its value and does not recover it from the principal unless the agent ordered him to take for bargaining; then when the agent is liable, he recovers from the principal. End quote. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He erred and delivered non-sold goods and they perished; he is liable for the value because he took possession in the manner of sale. He sent a messenger to the clothier and said: Send me such a garment. The clothier sent it with him or with another, and the garment was lost before reaching the orderer, and they agreed on that; there is no liability on the messenger. Then if he is the messenger of the orderer, the liability is on the orderer; if he is the messenger of the clothier, there is no liability on anyone, but when it reaches the orderer, the orderer is liable. Likewise if he sent to another and said: Send me ten dirhams as a loan, and he sent, then the orderer is liable if he acknowledges that he is his messenger. If he sent it with someone other than his messenger, there is no liability on the orderer before it arrives. Likewise the creditor, if he sent a messenger to collect his debt, [????] the second becomes a sale. End quote. He said: (It is not correct because of what is in al-Khaniyyah etc.) He said in al-Nahr: We do not accept that it is not correct, for al-Tarsusi did not mention it by way of legal reasoning but by transmission from the scholars stated in al-Muntaqa; and he gave the reason in al-Muhit that by implication he became satisfied with the sale, interpreting his statement as being for righteousness and rectification. And he attributed it in al-Khazanah to al-Muntaqa, but he said: In analogy, the value is obligatory. Al-Tarsusi said: It should not exceed the named amount, as in the case of a void lease, but there is a problem; rather the full value should be obligatory, and they have explicitly stated that in void sales, so too here. End quote from al-Nahr. I say: What the author transmitted from al-Khaniyyah is not refuted, because the bargainer, when he consumes the garment, becomes satisfied with the mentioned price, so the sale is valid with the price, unlike the consumption by his heir, because the heir is not a contracting party. So the author's statement 'the heir is like the inheritor' is denied. It is supported by what al-Tarsusi mentioned from al-Muntaqa: If he said to another, 'Take this garment for twenty,' and the buyer said, 'I will take it for ten,' and he took the garment and destroyed it in his hand, he must pay its value because he took possession in the manner of sale and with a price. If he consumed it, he must pay twenty because by consumption the sale becomes final with the named price by implication, interpreting his action as being for righteousness and rectification. If the seller said, 'I retract what I said,' or one of them died before the buyer said 'I am satisfied,' the manner of sale is nullified; then if the buyer consumes it after that, he must pay its value, just as in real sale, if it is nullified, the sold item remains in his hand as a trust, so here too. End quote. Since the sale is nullified, how can the heir be like the inheritor? Because the contract was between the seller and the inheritor, and the sale was nullified by his death, so the sold item becomes a pure trust in the hand of the heir. If he consumes it, he must pay its value, unlike the consumption by the inheritor, because that is consent to confirm the contract. This is understood from the statement of al-Khaniyyah: 'Likewise if the heir of the purchaser consumed it, etc.' For it indicates that if the inheritor consumed it, it is not like the consumption of the heir; rather he must pay the price, as we said.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the liability for goods taken for bargaining (سوم الشراء). The author refutes al-Tarsusi's view that if the goods perish, the value is due, but if consumed, the named price is due. The author argues that this is incorrect based on texts from al-Khaniyyah and other works. The correct position is that if the buyer consumes the goods, he is liable for the named price because his consumption implies consent to the sale. However, if the goods perish or if the heir consumes them after the buyer's death, the liability is for the market value, not the named price, because the heir is not a party to the sale. The passage also discusses the agent's liability and the messenger's role. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that consumption by the original buyer establishes the sale at the named price, while consumption by the heir or perishing requires payment of the value.

Key Terms
المقبوض على سوم الشراء (al-maqbood 'ala sawm al-shira'): Goods taken into possession for the purpose of negotiating a purchase, with a price stated.
الضمان (al-daman): Legal liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property in one's possession.
القيمة (al-qeema): Market value of the goods at the time of loss or consumption.
الثمن (al-thaman): The named price agreed upon during bargaining.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, if a buyer consumes goods taken for bargaining with a stated price, what is the liability?
A) He pays the market value.
B) He pays the named price.
C) He pays nothing because the sale was not finalized.
D) He pays the price only if the seller demands it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, consumption of goods taken for bargaining by the original buyer binds the sale at the named price; otherwise, liability is for market value.

Liability for Goods Taken for Bargaining
Ruling with proof from al-Bazzaziyyah on bargaining liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a person is liable for goods taken for bargaining and explain why a stipulation of no liability is invalid.

Core Idea
For goods taken for bargaining, liability is incurred only if the price is stated.

This lesson unpacks a classic Hanafi ruling: when does someone who takes an item to consider buying it become liable for its loss? The answer hinges on whether a price has been agreed. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the conditions using examples from al-Bazzaziyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is taking possession of goods for bargaining (sawm al-shira'). The default is that the goods are held as a trust (amanah) with no liability unless a condition changes it.
Trust means the holder is not liable for loss unless negligence is proven.
2
Determine when liability arises
Liability arises when the price (thaman) is explicitly stated. If the price is fixed, the possessor becomes a guarantor (damin) even if he stipulates no liability.
The condition is 'if its price is stated' (idha bayyana thamanahu).
3
Analyze the proof from al-Bazzaziyyah
The bow example: a person asks to buy a bow, the price is fixed, he draws it with permission and it breaks. He is liable for the value. If the price was not fixed, no liability.
The stipulation 'no liability' is invalid because the basis of liability is the price agreement.
4
Apply the Imam's additional rulings
Abu Hanifa adds: if someone shows a dirham and the person presses it, or a bow and draws it, or a garment and tears it, he is liable unless he was ordered to do so. But if the act is necessary for examination, he is not liable unless he exceeds.
The possessor is believed in his claim that he did not exceed proper examination.
5
Conclude the ruling
The mufta bihi position: for bargaining, liability follows when the price is stated; otherwise the goods remain a trust.
This is from the later Hanafi compilations (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فبعث معه يرى وضاع يكون من مال الدائن، وإن مع الآخر لا حتى يصل إليه اهـ. ثم اعلم أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء إذا بين ثمنه مضمون وإن اشترط أن لا ضمان فيه لما في البزازية : استباع قوساً وتقرر الثمن فمده بإذن البائع أو قال له إن انكسر فلا ضمان عليك فمده وانكسر يضمن قيمته، وإن لم يتقرر الثمن فلا ضمان ولو بالإذن لأن اشتراط عدم الضمان في المقبوض على السوم باطل وعن الإمام أراه الدرهم لينظر إليه فغمزه أو قوساً فمده فانكسر أو ثوباً فتخرق ضمن إن لم يأمره بالغمز والمد واللبس، وقيل إن كان لا إلا بالغمز لا يضمن إن لم يجاوز ويصدق في أنه لم يجاوز اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين: المقبوض على سوم الرهن مضمون بالأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، وما قبض على سوم القرض مضمون بما ساوم كمقبوض على حقيقته بمنزلة مقبوض على سوم البيع إلا أن في البيع يضمن القيمة وهنا يهلك الرهن بما ساومه من القرض، وما قبض على سوم النكاح مضمون يعني لو قبض أمة غيره ليتزوجها بإذن مولاها فهلكت في يده ضمن قيمتها والمهر قبل تسليمه مضمون، وكذا بدل الخلع في يد المرأة يعني لو تزوجها على عين أو خالعها فهلكت قبل قبضه يلزمه مثله في المثلي وقيمته في القيمي .اهـ. ذكره في الثلاثين منه .
He sent with him to be seen, and it was lost; it is from the property of the creditor. And if with another, not until it reaches him. End quote. Then know that what is taken for bargaining (sawm al-shira') if its price is stated, it is liable even if he stipulates that there is no liability, because of what is in al-Bazzaziyyah: He asked to buy a bow and the price was fixed; he drew it with the seller's permission, or he said, 'If it breaks, there is no liability on you,' so he drew it and it broke; he is liable for its value. If the price was not fixed, there is no liability even with permission, because stipulating absence of liability for what is taken for bargaining is invalid. And from the Imam: He showed him a dirham to look at it, and he pressed it, or a bow and he drew it and it broke, or a garment and it tore; he is liable if he did not order him to press, draw, or wear. It is said that if it is not except by pressing, he is not liable if he did not exceed, and he is believed in that he did not exceed. End quote. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: What is taken for pledging (sawm al-rahni) is liable for the lesser of its value and the debt. What is taken for lending (sawm al-qard) is liable for what was negotiated, like what is taken for its reality, just like what is taken for bargaining, except that in sale he is liable for the value, and here the pledge perishes for what he negotiated from the loan. What is taken for marriage (sawm al-nikah) is liable, meaning if he took possession of someone else's slave-girl to marry her with her master's permission, and she perished in his hand, he is liable for her value; and the dowry before delivery is liable. Likewise, the khul' compensation in the woman's hand means if he marries her on a specific item or divorces by khul', and it perishes before he takes possession, he must pay its like if fungible, and its value if non-fungible. End quote. He mentioned it in the thirtieth [section] of it.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on the liability for goods taken for various purposes, as compiled from al-Bazzaziyyah and Jami' al-Fusulayn. The key principle is that possession for bargaining (sawm al-shira') makes the goods a trust until consumed, but if the price is stated, the possessor is liable even if he stipulates no liability. For goods taken for pledge (sawm al-rahni), liability is for the lesser of the value and the debt. For goods taken for a loan (sawm al-qard), liability is for the amount negotiated. For goods taken for marriage (sawm al-nikah), if the slave-girl dies, the prospective husband pays her value; the dowry is also liable before delivery. These rulings are based on transmitted texts from earlier Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms
المقبوض على سوم الشراء (al-maqbood 'ala sawm al-shira): Goods taken into possession for the purpose of bargaining (considering purchase).
المقبوض على سوم الشراء إذا بين ثمنه مضمون (idha bayyana thamanahu madhmun): If the price is stated, the goods are guaranteed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a person become liable for goods taken for bargaining?
A) Whenever he takes possession with the seller's permission.
B) Only if the price is stated.
C) Only if he signs a contract.
D) Only if the goods are destroyed due to his negligence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, possession for bargaining becomes a guarantee only when a price is explicitly stated.

Liability for Goods Taken for Pledge, Loan, and Marriage
Rulings from Jami' al-Fusulayn on liability for pledge, loan, and marriage possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the liability amount for goods taken for pledge, loan, and marriage according to the Hanafi school as derived from Jami' al-Fusulayn.

Core Idea
Pledge liability is the lesser of value and debt; loan liability is the negotiated amount; marriage liability is the market value.

This lesson covers three more types of possession with purpose: pledge (sawm al-rahni), loan (sawm al-qard), and marriage (sawm al-nikah). The passage from Jami' al-Fusulayn provides clear formulas for each. Understanding these distinctions is essential for commercial and family transactions in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of possession
They are: pledge (sawm al-rahni), loan (sawm al-qard), and marriage (sawm al-nikah). Each has a specific liability rule.
2
State the rule for pledge (sawm al-rahni)
Liability is the lesser of the item's market value and the debt amount. This protects the pledgor from compensating more than the debt.
If value is 100 and debt is 50, liability is 50. If value is 30 and debt is 50, liability is 30.
3
State the rule for loan (sawm al-qard)
Liability is exactly the amount that was negotiated for the loan. The goods are treated as if they were actually taken in exchange for that amount.
Analogous to sale but here the liability is the negotiated sum.
4
State the rule for marriage (sawm al-nikah)
If a man takes a slave-girl to marry her with her owner's permission and she dies, he is liable for her market value (qimah). The dowry (mahr) before delivery is also liable.
5
Note the additional ruling on dowry and khul'
The dowry and khul' compensation are liable if the item perishes before delivery: pay like (mithl) for fungibles, value (qimah) for non-fungibles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فبعث معه يرى وضاع يكون من مال الدائن، وإن مع الآخر لا حتى يصل إليه اهـ. ثم اعلم أن المقبوض على سوم الشراء إذا بين ثمنه مضمون وإن اشترط أن لا ضمان فيه لما في البزازية : استباع قوساً وتقرر الثمن فمده بإذن البائع أو قال له إن انكسر فلا ضمان عليك فمده وانكسر يضمن قيمته، وإن لم يتقرر الثمن فلا ضمان ولو بالإذن لأن اشتراط عدم الضمان في المقبوض على السوم باطل وعن الإمام أراه الدرهم لينظر إليه فغمزه أو قوساً فمده فانكسر أو ثوباً فتخرق ضمن إن لم يأمره بالغمز والمد واللبس، وقيل إن كان لا إلا بالغمز لا يضمن إن لم يجاوز ويصدق في أنه لم يجاوز اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين: المقبوض على سوم الرهن مضمون بالأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، وما قبض على سوم القرض مضمون بما ساوم كمقبوض على حقيقته بمنزلة مقبوض على سوم البيع إلا أن في البيع يضمن القيمة وهنا يهلك الرهن بما ساومه من القرض، وما قبض على سوم النكاح مضمون يعني لو قبض أمة غيره ليتزوجها بإذن مولاها فهلكت في يده ضمن قيمتها والمهر قبل تسليمه مضمون، وكذا بدل الخلع في يد المرأة يعني لو تزوجها على عين أو خالعها فهلكت قبل قبضه يلزمه مثله في المثلي وقيمته في القيمي .اهـ. ذكره في الثلاثين منه .
He sent with him to be seen, and it was lost; it is from the property of the creditor. And if with another, not until it reaches him. End quote. This passage provides rulings on the liability for goods taken for various purposes, as compiled from al-Bazzaziyyah and Jami' al-Fusulayn. These rulings are based on transmitted texts from earlier Hanafi authorities.

المقبوض على سوم القرض (al-maqbood 'ala sawm al-qard): Goods taken into possession for the purpose of obtaining a loan.
المقبوض على سوم النكاح (al-maqbood 'ala sawm al-nikah): A woman (slave-girl) taken into possession for the purpose of marriage.

A) The full market value of the goods.

Key Takeaway

Liability for Goods Taken for Marriage: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on liability for goods taken for marriage and explain the legal reasoning behind each, including the role of muqaddar shar'an.

Core Idea
A legally determined dowry is treated as named, so liability attaches even without explicit naming.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding liability for a slave-girl taken for marriage (sawm al-nikah). The key question is whether naming the dowry is necessary for the possessor to be liable if she perishes. Two positions emerge: one analogizes to sale, requiring naming; the other argues that the dowry is legally determined (muqaddar shar'an) and thus counts as named. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between contractual and legally determined obligations in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling on buyer's option
First, identify the matn's ruling: the buyer's option (khiyar al-mushtari) does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership. Ownership transfers immediately, subject to rescission.
This sets the context: the passage moves from a settled principle to a disputed extension.
2
Identify the issue of sawm al-nikah
The passage turns to a new case: goods taken for marriage (sawm al-nikah). The matn states they are liable. The dispute is whether this liability depends on naming the dowry.
Note that this is an extension from sale to marriage, requiring qiyas or a separate principle.
3
Present the first position: analogy to sale
Some scholars argue by qiyas: just as in bargaining (sawm al-shira'), liability requires naming the price, so in marriage, liability requires naming the dowry. Without naming, there is no liability.
This position relies on the qiyas rule and the fatwa on bargaining.
4
Present the second position: legal determination
The author (Ibn Nujaym?) argues that the dowry is legally determined (muqaddar shar'an), so it is treated as named. Therefore, liability is absolute, whether or not the dowry is explicitly named. He supports this with the validity of marriage without a named dowry.
Key evidence: marriage with 'no dowry' is valid, and proper dowry (mahr al-mithl) applies, unlike sale where 'no price' is void.
5
Analyze the rebuttal and thamarah
Some scholars reject this distinction, claiming it is not clear. The practical consequence (thamarah) is clear: in a case where a man takes a woman for marriage without naming a dowry and she dies, one view requires payment of her value, the other requires nothing.
The author leans toward absolute liability but admits no explicit transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وخيار المشتري لا يمنع ولا يملك أي لا يمنع خروج المبيع عن ملك البائع فيخرج عن ملكه للزومه من جهة لا من خيار له، فلو أعتقه البائع لم يصح إعتاقه، ولو وما قبض على سوم النكاح مضمون (الخ قال بعض الفضلاء : ظاهره أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون المهر مسمى أو لا. ولقائل أن يقول هذا إذا كان المهر مسمى قياساً على المقبوض على سوم الشراء فإنه لا يكون مضموناً إلا بعد تسمية الثمن على ما عليه الفتوى فيكون المقبوض على سوم النكاح مضموناً إذا كان المهر مسمى وإلا فلا، ولم أر في المسألة نقلاً غير أن إطلاق العبارة يقتضي الضمان مطلقاً إلا أن يوجد نقل صريح بخلافه، وعليه فيحتاج للفرق بينهما فإنه لا يضمن إلا بعد تسمية الثمن، وكذا المقبوض على سوم الرهن فإنه لا يكون مضموناً إلا إذا . سمى ما يرهن به في الأصح فيحتاج إلى الفرق بينهما أيضاً. قال : وقد ظهر لي فرق بين المقبوض على سوم الشراء والمقبوض على سوم الرهن وبين المقبوض على سوم النكاح وهو أن المهر مقدر شرعاً من حيث هو والمقدر شرعاً مسمى شرعاً والمسمى شرعاً معتبر مطلقاً ألا أنه لو تزوج على أن لا مهر صح ويجب مهر المثل، ولو اشترى على أن لا ثمن كان تری باطلاً اعتباراً للتسمية الشرعية في المهر، ولذا كان المقبوض على سوم النكاح مضموناً، سواء سمى المهر أو لا، لأنه مسمى شرعاً فاعتبر ذلك لوجوب الضمان بخلاف الثمن وما يرهن به فإن ذلك غير مقدر شرعاً فلا بد من التسمية لوجوب الضمان فيها اهـ ورده بعض الفضلاء قائلاً: لم يظهر لي هذا
His saying: (The buyer's option does not prevent and does not own) i.e., it does not prevent the sold item from leaving the ownership of the seller, so it leaves his ownership due to its being binding from one aspect, not from the option. So if the seller frees [a slave], his freeing is not valid. And if... And what is taken for marriage (sawm al-nikah) is liable (etc.) Some scholars said: Its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between whether the dowry is named or not. And one may say: This is when the dowry is named, by analogy to what is taken for bargaining, for it is not liable except after naming the price, according to the fatwa. So what is taken for marriage is liable if the dowry is named, otherwise not. I have not seen a transmission on this issue except that the absolute wording implies liability absolutely, unless a clear transmission to the contrary is found. Thus, one needs to differentiate between them: it is not liable except after naming the price. Likewise, what is taken for pledging (sawm al-rahni) is not liable except if he names what he pledges with, according to the soundest view. So one needs to differentiate between them as well. He said: A difference has become clear to me between what is taken for bargaining and for pledging, and what is taken for marriage: that the dowry is legally determined (muqaddar shar'an) in itself; what is legally determined is considered as named legally, and what is legally named is considered absolutely. However, if he marries with the stipulation of no dowry, it is valid and the proper dowry is obligatory. If he buys with the stipulation of no price, it is considered void, due to the consideration of the legal naming in the dowry. Therefore, what is taken for marriage is liable whether the dowry is named or not, because it is legally named, so that is considered for the obligation of liability, unlike the price and what is pledged, because those are not legally determined, so naming is necessary for the obligation of liability therein. End quote. And some scholars refuted this saying: This is not clear to me.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage begins with a commentary on the matn phrase 'وخيار المشتري لا يمنع ولا يملك' which means the buyer's option does not prevent the sale from being binding on the seller's side, so ownership transfers from the seller immediately. Then the passage delves into a dispute about whether goods taken for marriage (sawm al-nikah) are liable without naming the dowry. Some scholars argue by analogy with bargaining (sawm al-shira') that the dowry must be named for liability. However, one scholar (possibly the author) argues that the dowry is legally determined (muqaddar shar'an), so it is treated as named even if not explicitly stated. Therefore, liability applies whether the dowry is named or not. Another scholar rejects this distinction. The passage thus presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the issue.

Key Terms
خيار المشتري (khiyar al-mushtari): The option of the buyer to rescind the sale within a stipulated period.
المقبوض على سوم النكاح (al-maqbood 'ala sawm al-nikah): A woman (slave-girl) taken into possession by a man with the intention of marrying her, with the master's permission.
مقدر شرعاً (muqaddar shar'an): Legally determined; a quantity or value that is fixed by Islamic law rather than by agreement of the parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the key difference between the dowry (mahr) and the price in a sale that justifies absolute liability for sawm al-nikah?
A) The dowry is always a fixed amount, unlike price.
B) The dowry is legally determined (muqaddar shar'an), while the price is not.
C) Marriage is a contract of exchange, while sale is not.
D) The dowry must be named at the time of the contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the legal determination of the dowry (muqaddar shar'an) means it is treated as named, making liability for goods taken for marriage absolute, unlike sale or pledge where naming is required.
